Chapter 1
Notation and Conventions

1.1 Scope and authority
This chapter is normative for the entire project. Every quantity that appears in this document, in the source code, in the SRLOG binary log, and in any public API follows the conventions dened here. Where an external reference uses a dierent convention, the transcription into this project's convention is stated explicitly at the point of use. The attitude conventions in Section 1.4 ratify project decision D-7.

1.2 Reference frames
Frames are denoted by single calligraphic letters used as sub- and superscripts on vectors and direction-cosine matrices. The frames used across the project are listed in Table 1.1. In Phase 1 only the GCRF is exercised; the remaining frames are named now so that channel and API labels are stable, and each is dened rigorously in the chapter of the phase that introduces it.

1.3 Vectors, matrices, and the DCM convention

Physical vectors are set in bold italic, r, and matrices in bold upright-italic capitals, C . The coordinates of a vector resolved in frame A are written rA. The skew-symmetric cross-product matrix of a = [a1, a2, a3]T is

1.4.3 Mandatory note: mapping to Eigen::Quaterniond
The C++ core represents quaternions with Eigen::Quaterniond [18], whose
component ordering diers between its constructor and its internal storage. This mismatch is the single most likely source of attitude-convention defects, so the mapping is spelled out here and is binding on all core and binding code:
 The value constructor takes the scalar rst : Eigen::Quaterniond(w,
x, y, z).
 The internal coecient storage, exposed by .coeffs(), orders the
scalar last : [x, y, z, w].

1.5 Units
All quantities are SI throughout the core, the logs, and the APIs; no non-SI unit crosses any interface. In this document, numerical values with units
are typeset with the siunitx package, for example ṁ = 3.986 004 418 Ṫ 1014 m3 s-2, the geocentric gravitational constant (TCB-compatible value)
of the IERS Conventions (2010) [47]. Conguration keys and log channel
names carry their unit as a sux (thrust_vac_N, r_m, v_mps, w_b_radps, mass_kg, t_s) so that a wrong unit is visible at the point of use. Angles are
radians in code and logs; degrees appear only in human-facing conguration
keys explicitly suxed _deg.
Epochs in conguration les are UTC ISO-8601 strings. The internal timescale (TAI, decision D-6) and all timescale conversions are dened in the Phase 2 time-systems chapter.

Chapter 2
Two-Body Point-Mass Placeholder Model
2.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the Phase 1 placeholder dynamics model: a spacecraft treated as a massless test particle under the point-mass gravity of a single central body, integrated with the classical fourth-order RungeKutta method. The model exists to exercise the complete pipeline  mission conguration, the C++ core, the SRLOG writer, the Python loader, and the determinism gates  before any production physics lands, and to establish the mandatory chapter template and equation-label-to-code traceability discipline that every subsequent model chapter follows. It is implemented in
cpp/src/models/twobody.cpp.
2.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions: 1. The central body is a point mass or, equivalently by Newton's shell theorem, a spherically symmetric mass distribution; its gravitational
eld is characterized entirely by the parameter ṁ = GM .
2. The spacecraft is a test particle: its mass is negligible relative to the
central body (m  M ) and does not inuence the motion; the logged
mass is constant.
7

3. No perturbations act: no gravity-eld harmonics, no third-body gravity, no atmospheric drag, no solar radiation pressure, no thrust.

4. No attitude dynamics are modeled. The logged attitude channels carry
the xed identity quaternion [ 1, 0, 0, 0 ] (scalar-rst, per Chapter 1)
and zero angular rate; they exist to establish the log schema, not to represent physics.

Domain of validity: pipeline and infrastructure testing, determinism gat-

ing, and Keplerian reference cases for which an analytic solution exists. The

not model is

valid for mission analysis of any real orbit regime.

Out-of-domain behavior: the model silently omits every perturbing accel-

eration, so its error against a real trajectory grows secularly  for example,
Earth-orbit nodal regression driven by the J2 zonal harmonic (on the or-

der of degrees per day in low Earth orbit) is entirely absent. There is no

in-model detection of this condition; the guard is procedural, namely that

Phase 3 perturbation models supersede this chapter's dynamics for any pro-

duction study, and this placeholder remains selectable only as an explicit

conguration choice.

2.3 Derivation

The derivation follows the standard two-body development; see Vallado [57]
for the classical treatment. Let two bodies of masses M (central body) and m (spacecraft) have inertial positions RM I and RmI , and dene the relative position r = RmI - RM I with r = r. Newton's law of universal gravitation
gives the force on the spacecraft due to the central body as

GM m r

2.4 Discretization and implementation

Equation (2.4) is integrated as the autonomous rst-order system

y=

r v

,

v y = f (y) = - ṁ r/ r3 ,

(2.8)

using the shared xed-step classical fourth-order RungeKutta method of
the integrator library, equation (7.5) in Chapter 7, with xed step h = t, local truncation error O(h5), and global error O(h4) [20]. The model
contributes only the right-hand side of equation (2.8); stepping, convergenceorder evidence, and dense output are the integrator chapter's responsibility. Because the system is autonomous, the time argument passed through the integrator interface does not enter the stage evaluations.
Implementation notes:

9

1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/twobody.cpp.
The source comments echo the labels eq:twobody:accel (the acceleration evaluation) and eq:twobody:firstorder (the right-hand-side
assembly) verbatim, so each code block traces to its dening equation
and the chapter-manifest lint can hold code and document together.

2. Gravitational parameter. The Earth value is ṁ = 3.986 004 418 Ṫ
1014 m3 s-2, from the IERS Conventions (2010), Technical Note No. 36 [47]. The constant is dened once in the core (exposed as _core.gm("earth"))
and cited at its denition.

3. Determinism. The integration loop is single-threaded with a xed

evaluation order, compiled with fast-math disabled and oating-point

contraction o (decision D-10), so the same inputs on the same binary

V001 reproduce bit-identical trajectories  the property gated by test

.

Logging. 4.

States are recorded at the congured truth rate by decima-

tion of integrator steps: the state is logged at t = 0 and at every k-th

truth step thereafter, where k = 1/(t Ṗ f

) is validated to be an exact

positive integer. Logged values are never interpolated.

Chapter 3
Time Systems
3.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the time-system module (FR-2, decision D-6): the internal two-part TAI epoch representation, the conversion between UTC calendar elds and TAI through a bundled, versioned leap-second table, the exact oset to Terrestrial Time (TT), and the truncated periodic series for Barycentric Dynamical Time (TDB). Every downstream Phase 2 model consumes these scales: the Earth-orientation frame chain is a function of UT1 and TT, and the ephemeris evaluator is a function of TDB. The module is im-
plemented in cpp/src/time.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/time.hpp;
per decision D-2 the core accepts only numeric calendar elds  ISO-8601 text parsing lives in the Python frontend.
3.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Constant-oset UTC era only. UTC is related to TAI by an integer
number of seconds, which holds from 1972-01-01 onward. The pre-1972 rubber second era (frequency osets and fractional jumps) is out of domain.
2. Leap-second knowledge horizon. The bundled table encodes the
published TAI-UTC step history through the step eective 2017-0101 (AT = 37 s) and is veried against IERS Bulletin C 71 (January
2026), which announced that no leap second is introduced at the end
not of June 2026 [26]. The rst UTC date at which a leap second
12

present in the table could take eect is therefore 2027-01-01 (the endof-December-2026 insertion opportunity, which Bulletin C 71 does not rule out).
3. Positive leap seconds only. Every leap second since 1972 has been
an insertion; the table holds only +1 steps and the conversion logic renders only inserted seconds (second 60). A negative leap second
would require a table and code revision.
4. Proleptic Gregorian calendar. Calendar dates map to day num-
bers by the integer Julian Day Number algorithm of Fliegel and Van Flandern [14], exact over the module domain (veried exhaustively over 19722068 at golden generation).
5. Geocentric TDB. The TDB-TT series carries only the time-dependent
terms; topocentric terms (observer longitude and geocentric distance,
< 2.1 ṁs at the geoid) are omitted, consistent with the D-6 accuracy
budget.
Domain of validity: UTC epochs from 1972-01-01 onward; full leap-
second accuracy through 2026-12-31; TDB-TT within the D-6 budget of 30 ṁs over 16002200 (section 3.3).
Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly:
 Calendar input before 1972-01-01, an invalid eld (month, day, hour, minute out of range; non-nite seconds), or second  60 outside an inserted leap second throws std::domain_error (surfaced in Python as ValueError). An invalid instant is never silently normalized, because
normalizing would shift the epoch by up to one second.
accepted  Calendar input on or after the table expiry (2027-01-01) is
with the last tabulated oset (AT = 37 s). The core exposes the table
version and expiry programmatically and the Python frontend emits a warning for such epochs; the decision is placed in Python because the core never reads the clock (D-2) and cannot know whether its table is stale.
3.3 Derivation
3.3.1 Time scales
International Atomic Time (TAI) is the continuous atomic scale, one SI second per second on the rotating geoid; it has no leap seconds, so every
13

TAI day spans exactly 86 400 s. Coordinated Universal Time (UTC) diers
from TAI by an integer step count,

TAI = UTC + AT (t),

(3.1)

where AT is the tabulated leap-second oset, constant between steps that
take eect at UTC midnights announced by IERS Bulletin C [26]. Terrestrial Time is dened with a constant oset from TAI (IAU 1991 Resolution A4, as stated by Kaplan [29]):

TT = TAI + 32.184 s exactly.

(3.2)

The J2000 reference epoch is the instant
J2000 = 2000-01-01T12:00:00.0 TT = JD 2451545.0 TT = 2000-01-01T11:59:27.816 TAI,
(3.3) the TAI clock face following from equation (3.2).

3.3.2 Two-part TAI epoch
An epoch is stored as the pair (d, s)  whole TAI days d and TAI seconds of day s  [0, 86400)  counted from 2000-01-01T00:00:00.0 TAI, so J2000 is the pair (0, 43167.816) by equation (3.3). Because TT and TAI dier
by a constant, elapsed TT equals elapsed TAI, and the TT Julian-century argument used by the TDB series and the frame models is

86400 d + s - 43167.816 T=
86400 Ṗ 36525

[Julian centuries since J2000 TT].
(3.4)

The two-part split is the load-bearing design decision of D-6. A single
binary64 count of seconds since J2000 reaches  1.9 Ṫ 109 by 2060, where its quantum (one unit in the last place) is 2-52 Ṫ 231  2.4 Ṫ 10-7 s  incompatible with the  1 Ṫ 10-8 s of UT1 precision the Earth-rotation-angle computation requires (1 Ṫ 10-8 s of UT1 is  7 Ṫ 10-12 rad of rotation). In

the two-part form the day count is exact and the sub-day part never ex-
ceeds 86 400 s, whose quantum is 2-52 Ṫ 217 = 1.455 Ṫ 10-11 s, uniform over

the whole 20202060 span  three orders of magnitude below the require-

ment. Downstream consumers preserve this by dierencing or reducing the

parts separately (never summing them rst), exactly as the validation tests

compare two-part Julian Dates.

14

3.3.3 Calendar mapping
Gregorian calendar dates map to integer day numbers by the machine algorithm of Fliegel and Van Flandern [14], which computes the Julian Day Number with truncating integer division,
a = (m - 14) /12, JDN(y, m, d) = d - 32075 + 1461 (y + 4800 + a)/4 + 367 (m - 2 - 12a)/12
- 3 (y + 4900 + a)/100 /4,
(3.5)
with every division truncated toward zero; the epoch day count is N = JDN - 2451545 since JDN(2000-01-01) = 2451545. The companion inverse algorithm from the same reference recovers (y, m, d) from N . Both directions
were veried exhaustively against an independent implementation for every day from 1972-01-01 through 2068-12-31 at golden generation.
3.3.4 UTC to TAI and back, including leap seconds
For UTC calendar elds (y, m, d, h, min , sutc) the UTC seconds of day are  = 3600h + 60 min + sutc, and by equation (3.1) the epoch is
A = 86400 N (y, m, d)++AT (y, m, d), dTAI = A/86400, sTAI = A-86400 dTAI,
(3.6)
where A is TAI seconds since 2000-01-01T00:00:00 TAI. During an inserted leap second the seconds eld satises sutc  [60, 61), so   [86400, 86401)
and the mapping continues smoothly across the insertion  no special case is needed in the forward direction beyond admitting the extended seconds range on exactly the nal minute of a day the table steps after.
For the inverse, observe that the UTC civil day with epoch day num-
ber D begins at A = 86400 D + AT (D) and ends where the next day begins, so its TAI duration is 86400 + [AT (D+1) - AT (D)] seconds: 86 401 s for a day ending in an inserted leap second. Given (dTAI, sTAI), the containing UTC day is dTAI itself when sTAI  AT (dTAI) and the preceding day otherwise, and the UTC seconds of day are  = A - 86400 D - AT (D). The value   [86400, 86401) arises exactly when the preceding
day ends in an inserted second and the instant lies inside it; it is rendered
as 23:59:60+fraction. The round trip is therefore the identity for every valid
UTC instant, including instants inside a leap second  the property gated
by time_leap_second_roundtrip.
15

3.3.5 TDB
Barycentric Dynamical Time diers from TT by periodic relativistic terms. The module implements the seven-term truncation of the Fairhead and Bretagnon series [12] as given by Kaplan [29, eq. 2.6]:
TDB - TT [s] = 0.001657 sin(628.3076 T + 6.2401) + 0.000022 sin(575.3385 T + 4.2970) + 0.000014 sin(1256.6152 T + 6.1969) + 0.000005 sin(606.9777 T + 4.0212) + 0.000005 sin(52.9691 T + 0.4444) + 0.000002 sin(21.3299 T + 5.5431) + 0.000010 T sin(628.3076 T + 4.2490),
(3.7)
with T from equation (3.4) (using TT rather than TDB in the argument perturbs the result below 1 Ṫ 10-12 s and is the form Kaplan gives). Kaplan quotes  10 ṁs accuracy against the full model over 16002200 [29], inside the D-6 budget of 30 ṁs; the observed maximum against the full FairheadBretagnon model (ERFA eraDtdb) over the golden epochs spanning 20072060 is 5.54 Ṫ 10-6 s (tests/golden/time/manifest.toml). The dominant term is the annual aberration of the terrestrial clock (k sin g with g
the Earth's mean anomaly); truncation is acceptable because the ephemeris consumer tolerates tens of microseconds of argument error (interplanetary
velocities of  40 km s-1 make 30 ṁs about 1.2 mm of position).
3.4 Discretization and implementation
1. Module and traceability. The conversions live in cpp/src/time.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:time:j2000, eq:time:fvf, eq:time:utc2tai, eq:time:tai2utc, eq:time:tt, eq:time:ttcent, and eq:time:tdb verbatim.
2. Exact integer bookkeeping. Equations (3.5) and (3.6) are eval-
uated in 64-bit integer arithmetic for every whole-second quantity; the fractional second is split o exactly (the fractional part of a binary64 is itself representable) and rides through unchanged. The single rounding step in a UTC-to-TAI conversion is the nal addition
sTAI = fl(isod + frac), whose error is at most 2-37  7.3 Ṫ 10-12 s (one half ulp at 86 400 s). Consequently the UTC  TAI  UTC
round trip is bit-exact whenever the fractional second is representable at that quantum (all golden inputs use dyadic fractions), and within
1.5 Ṫ 10-11 s otherwise.
16

3. Leap-second table. The 28-entry TAI-UTC step history is a constexpr
array cited at its denition (IERS Bulletin C series, veried through Bulletin C 71 [26]), scanned with a xed-order loop (branch-stable, D-10). The table version string and expiry date (2027-01-01) are ex-
posed programmatically (leap_table_info) so the Python frontend
can warn on post-expiry epochs; the warning lives in Python because the core never reads the clock (D-2).

4. Epoch arithmetic. tai_add_seconds restores the 0  s < 86400
invariant by whole-day reduction plus at most one x-up per side (the oating oor at the boundary can be o by one ulp). Precision is
ulp(max(|t|, 86400)): exact nanosecond resolution for within-mission
osets, degrading gracefully for osets of years.

Determinism. 5.

All paths are straight-line integer and IEEE-754 dou-

ble arithmetic with xed evaluation order, compiled with fast-math

disabled and contraction o (D-10). The golden tests exploit this: the

committed reference values were generated by a Python implementa-

tion performing the identical operation sequence, and the C++ results

bit for bit are required to match them

(libm-dependent quantities 

the TDB sines  carry a documented 1 Ṫ 10-13 s tolerance instead).

6. Binding surface. Epochs cross the pybind11 boundary as plain (day,
sec) tuples; std::domain_error maps to Python ValueError. The
Python mission validator warns (never errors) on epochs past the table
expiry, so a stale table can never block a run, only annotate it.

scripts/lint_chapters.py; golden provenance and tolerances are recorded in tests/golden/time/manifest.toml.

Chapter 4
Rotation Kernel
4.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the rotation kernel (FR-3, decision D-7): Hamilton quaternion algebra, direction-cosine matrices (DCMs), the elementary frame
rotations R1, R2, R3, and the 3-2-1 and 3-1-3 Euler-angle sequences, to-
gether with all conversions among these representations. The kernel is the attitude substrate of the project: the Earth, Moon, and Mars frame constructions of Chapter 5 are compositions of its elementary rotations, and the Phase 4 attitude dynamics will integrate quaternions that this kernel
converts and normalizes. It is implemented in cpp/src/rotation.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/rotation.hpp; every convention below
restates and implements the notation chapter's ratication of decision D-7 (Section 1.4).
4.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Unit quaternions for attitude. Attitude operations (dcm_from_quat,
quat_transform) assume unit-norm input; quat_normalize provides
the projection and is exact to a few ulp. Normalizing a zero or non-
nite quaternion would fabricate an attitude, so it throws std::domain_error (surfaced in Python as ValueError) instead of defaulting.
2. Proper rotation matrices for extraction. The DCM-input func-
tions (quat_from_dcm, the Euler extractions) assume an orthonormal matrix with determinant +1. Orthonormality is a caller invariant,
20

maintained by construction everywhere in the core and gated by the
property tests (rotation_dcm_orthonormality_properties); it is not
re-checked per call inside the deterministic loop.

3. Double-precision conditioning near gimbal lock. Within an an-
in- gular distance  of an Euler sequence's singular middle angle, the dividual rst and third angles are ill-conditioned: an absolute matrix-

element perturbation of order the machine epsilon  produces angle

errors of order /, because the four elements that determine those

angles all carry a factor cos a2 (3-2-1) or sin a2 (3-1-3) of magnitude

rotation . The recomposed

degrades with the same O(/) envelope,

since the two ill-conditioned angle errors arise from independent matrix

elements and do not cancel. The implementation is tested against the
conservative envelope 100 / and observed at 25 / (Section 4.5).

Domain of validity: all of SO(3) for quaternion and DCM operations;
all of SO(3) for Euler composition; Euler extraction recovers individually
meaningful angles only away from the sequence's gimbal lock (|a2| = /2 for 3-2-1; a2  {0, } for 3-1-3), with the quantied degradation above inside
that neighborhood.
Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly:

 A non-orthonormal matrix passed to quat_from_dcm or an Euler ex-
traction returns the parameters of a nearby rotation without detection  there is no per-call orthonormality check (see assumption 2). The guard is upstream: every matrix produced by the core is orthonormal to machine precision by construction.

exact  At

gimbal lock (the singular elements identically zero) only the

sum or dierence of the rst and third angles is observable. The deter-
ministic policy is a1 = 0 with the whole degenerate rotation assigned to a3; the recomposed rotation is exact. There is no warning  the

policy is a documented convention, not an error.

 quat_normalize throws on zero or non-nite input (assumption 1); no
other kernel function throws.

4.3 Derivation
The conventions and closed forms follow Markley and Crassidis [35], transcribed to this project's scalar-rst component ordering; the notation chapter (Section 1.4) is the authoritative statement of the conventions themselves.

4.3.4 Robust quaternion extraction (Shepperd's method)

Taking traces and diagonal elements of equation (4.2) with qŸ = 1 gives

1 + tr CAB = 4qw2 , 1 + 2Cii - tr CAB = 4qi2 (i = x, y, z),

(4.8)

while the o-diagonal sums and dierences yield the mixed products, e.g.
C23 - C32 = 4qwqx and C12 + C21 = 4qxqy. Since the four quantities in

23

equation (4.8) sum to 4, the largest is at least 1; Shepperd's method [54]
computes that component by square root and the remaining three by division with the guaranteed-large denominator, so the extraction never divides by a small quantity and is numerically robust for every attitude  unlike the
trace-only formula, which cancels catastrophically near 180 rotations. The four golden cases shepperd_*_dominant make each component dominant in
turn, exercising all four branches.
4.3.5 Conditioning near gimbal lock
Let the input matrix carry absolute element perturbations of order  (the
rounding oor of any upstream computation, e.g. equation (4.2)). At angular
distance  from lock, the elements determining a1 and a3 have magnitude O()  each carries the factor cos a2 or sin a2  so the extracted angles err by O(/). Recomposition does not cancel these errors: the 3-2-1 element C22 = c3c1 + s3s2s1 depends on the error combination (e1 - e3) sin(a3 - a1) at lock, and e1, e3 derive from disjoint element sets. The end-to-end round-trip error is therefore bounded by K / with K of order unity; the validation evidence tests K = 100 as a conservative envelope and observes K  25
(Table 4.1). For uniformly random attitudes the probability of falling within
10-3 of lock is below 10-6 per draw, and the Phase 2 criterion-6a bound of 1 Ṫ 10-13 rad holds with two orders of margin over the observed worst case.
4.4 Discretization and implementation
1. Module and traceability. The kernel lives in cpp/src/rotation.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:rotations:hamprod, eq:rotations:quat2dcm, eq:rotations:r1r2r3, eq:rotations:shepperd, eq:rotations:e321, and eq:rotations:e313 verbatim.
2. Eigen storage mapping (D-7). Quaternions are stored as Eigen::Quaterniond,
whose constructor is scalar-rst while its internal coeffs() storage is
scalar-last; the mandatory mapping table and its two binding rules are in the notation chapter (Section 1.4.3). The binding layer emits quaternions scalar-rst through the named accessors exclusively. Eigen's
.toRotationMatrix() implements the active convention and would
return the transpose of equation (4.2); core code uses this kernel's
dcm_from_quat for frame transformations, never .toRotationMatrix().
3. One code path for vector transformation. quat_transform eval-
uates the sandwich through dcm_from_quat, so the DCM and the
24

quaternion action on vectors agree structurally rather than by test alone.

4. Explicit Hamilton product. quat_multiply writes out equation (4.1)
component by component rather than delegating to Eigen's operator*,
so the convention is visible at the code and immune to any upstream
semantic change; the golden tests pin the equivalence.

5. Sign conventions. quat_from_dcm returns qw  0; extractions are
therefore reproducible bit for bit (D-10). All compositions use xed evaluation order; there is no fast-math and no contraction (D-10 build ags).

6. Exact-lock branch. The Euler extractions branch to the lock policy

exactly only when the singular elements are

zero (the hypot of two

doubles vanishes only then); every other input takes the general branch,

whose conditioning is quantied above.

scripts/lint_chapters.py; golden provenance and tolerances are recorded in tests/golden/rotations/manifest.toml.

Chapter 5
Reference Frames
5.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the reference-frame module (FR-3): the CIO-based
transformation between the GCRF (I in Table 1.1) and the rotating Earthxed frame (E) using the IAU 2006/2000B precession-nutation model and the Earth rotation angle; the lunar principal-axis frame (L) realized from the DE 3-1-3 libration Euler angles; and the Mars body-xed frame (M ) from the
IAU Working Group 2015 rotational elements. These constructions orient every body-xed model of later phases  harmonic gravity elds, atmospheres, ground-track and launch-site geometry  and consume the time systems of Chapter 3 and the rotation kernel of Chapter 4. The module is implemented
in cpp/src/frames.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/frames.hpp.
5.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. IAU 2000B nutation suces. The 77-term IAU 2000B abridged
series delivers a celestial pole within 1 mas ( 4.8 Ṫ 10-9 rad) of the full IAU 2000A model over 19952050 [37]. A 1 mas pole error displaces an Earth-xed position by  3 cm at the surface  far below
the mission-analysis needs of this simulator. The free core nutation, unpredictable and of comparable sub-mas size, is unmodeled in both 2000A and 2000B.
2. Polar motion is neglected. The produced Earth-xed frame is
strictly the Terrestrial Intermediate Reference System: the nal polar-
28

motion rotation W (xp, yp, s) of the full IERS chain is omitted. Po-
lar motion is observed, not modeled; its magnitude is bounded by
|xp|, |yp|  0.6  2.9 Ṫ 10-6 rad [47], i.e. up to  18 m of surface dis-
placement. EOP time-series ingestion is a PRD non-goal; the omission is exactly this bounded rotation.
3. Constant, user-suppliable UT1 (default 0). UT1 is realized
as UT1 = UTC + UT1 with a constant oset. By construction of UTC, |UT1 - UTC| < 0.9 s, so the default UT1 = 0 bounds the Earth-rotation error by 0.9 s of spin: 0.9 s Ṫ 7.292 Ṫ 10-5 rad s-1  6.6 Ṫ 10-5 rad,  420 m at the surface. A user-supplied constant ap-
propriate to the mission epoch reduces the error to the UT1 drift accumulated across the mission window (of order milliseconds per day, i.e. decimetres per day at the surface).
4. Time plumbing. The TT argument of the precession-nutation series
comes from the two-part TAI epoch (Chapter 3); the Mars elements
use the D-6 truncated TDB. The TDB truncation error ( 30 ṁs, observed 5.5 Ṫ 10-6 s) enters Mars W through the rotation rate as  2.1 Ṫ 10-9 rad  below the physical accuracy of the rotational-
element model itself (mas level).
5. Moon PA assembly only. The lunar construction is the exact 3-1-3
composition of supplied libration angles; the angles themselves come from the DE440 ephemeris evaluator (a separate module), and their physical accuracy is that of DE440 [45].

Domain of validity: epochs from 1972 (the leap-table domain of Chap-

ter 3); model delity per assumption 1 holds over the published 19952050

comparison span and degrades gracefully outside it (the golden gates run

model-faithful to 2060 against the same model). The frame chain is

to IAU

2006/2000B at the 10-11 matrix-element level everywhere in 20202060; its

physical delity to the true Earth orientation is set by assumptions 2 and 3,

which dominate every other term.

Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: epochs before 1972-
01-01 throw std::domain_error from the time module (the UT1 realization needs AT ); epochs past the leap-table expiry use the last tabulated oset

with the Python-layer warning of Chapter 3. No function of this module

throws on its own.

29

5.3 Derivation

5.3.1 The CIO-based chain

The IERS Conventions (2010), Chapter 5 [47], factor the celestial-to-terrestrial
transformation as W (t) R3(ERA) QT(t), where Q(t) orients the Celestial In-

termediate Pole (CIP) and Origin (CIO) in the GCRS, ERA is the Earth
rotation angle, and W is polar motion. With W omitted (assumption 2)

and this project's frame-transformation DCM convention, the implemented

chain is

CIE = R3 ERA(UT1) CICIRS,

(5.1)

with CICIRS the celestial-to-intermediate matrix built from the CIP coordinates X, Y and the CIO locator s below.

5.3.2 IAU 2006 precession in FukushimaWilliams angles

The IAU 2006 (P03) precession [10] is parameterized by the four Fukushima
Williams angles [15, 59] Ÿ, Ÿ, Ÿ, A  polynomials in the TT Julian-century argument t of equation (3.4), with frame bias absorbed into the polyno-
mial constant terms. The bias-precession-nutation (NPB) matrix folds the
nutation components directly into two of the angles [59]:

MNPB = R1 -(A + ) R3 -(Ÿ + ) R1(Ÿ) R3(Ÿ),

(5.2)

using the elementary frame rotations of equation (4.3). The polynomial coef-
cients (and the IAU 2006 mean obliquity A) are tabulated in cpp/src/frames_series.hpp,
transcribed from the ERFA 2.0.1 reference source [33] implementing [10, 59].

5.3.3 IAU 2000B nutation

The abridged IAU 2000B model [37] evaluates 77 luni-solar terms on the
linear Delaunay arguments l, l, F, D,  (their truncation to linear polyno-
mials is part of the published model), plus xed osets standing in for the
truncated planetary terms:

 =

(Ak+Akt) sin k+Ak cos k +pl,

 =

(Bk+Bk t) cos k+Bk sin k +pl,

k

(5.3)

where k is the integer combination of the ve arguments for term k and the planetary osets are pl = -0.135 mas, pl = 0.388 mas (the Luzum val-

ues appropriate to applying frame bias, precession, and nutation separately,

as equation (5.2) does [37, 33]).

5.3.4 CIP coordinates, the CIO locator, and the intermediate matrix

5.3.5 Earth rotation angle
The Earth rotation angle is the dening linear function of the UT1 Julian-day
interval Tu from J2000 (Capitaine, Guinot & McCarthy [9]; IERS Conven-
tions (2010), eq. 5.15 [47]):
ERA(Tu) = 2 frac(Tu) + 0.7790572732640 + 0.00273781191135448 Tu ,
(5.7)
where frac(Tu) is taken from the two Julian-date parts separately before the small rate coecient multiplies the collapsed Tu  the arrangement that preserves the two-part precision (Section 5.4). UT1 itself is UT1 = TAI-AT +UT1 with AT from the leap table of Chapter 3 and constant UT1 per assumption 3.

5.3.6 Moon principal-axis frame
The DE-series lunar librations are published as the 3-1-3 Euler angles , , 
that carry the ICRF axes onto the lunar principal axes [45], so with the

31

sequence convention of equation (4.5),
CIL = R3() R1() R3().

(5.8)

The construction takes the three angles as plain arguments: the DE440
Chebyshev evaluator that interpolates them is a separate module, and the
assembly must not depend on it. Representative DE440 magnitudes ( small,   0.4 rad,  unbounded) are among the committed golden angle sets.

(Chapter 3), which is why the two-part epoch exists. The implemen-
tation forms UT1 as an exact whole-day part (JD 2451544.5 + d, ex-
act in binary64 over the table domain) plus a seconds-of-day fraction
(s - AT + UT1)/86400 with quantum  1.5 Ṫ 10-11 s, and equation (5.7) takes frac(Tu) from the parts separately; only the 2.7 Ṫ 10-3 rate coecient multiplies the collapsed Tu, suppressing its rounding by
the same factor. The fraction may be negative for epochs in the rst
AT seconds of a TAI day; the nal modular reduction normalizes the
angle.

5. One rotation kernel. Every matrix is composed from the R1/R2/R3
primitives of Chapter 4 (which match the SOFA sign convention), in the same association order as the reference routines; the Moon PA assembly is literally the kernel's 3-1-3 composition (asserted bit-identical
in frames_moon_pa_golden).

before modulo 360

the radian conversion, and W 's linear term is

erator; the TDB day count is formed as the exact two-part dierence
(jd1 - 2451545.0) + jd2 before the single collapse.

7. Where polar motion would go. The omitted W of the full IERS
chain would left-multiply equation (5.1); the cookbook cross-check test documents this by comparing against the published no-polar-motion matrix.

Chapter 6
Planetary and Lunar Ephemerides

6.1 Purpose

This chapter documents the ephemeris service (FR-4, decision D-8): the

positions and velocities of the Sun, the EarthMoon barycenter (EMB),

the Earth, the Moon, and the Venus, Mars, and Jupiter barycenters, plus

the lunar libration angles, over the span 20202060, for use by the force

models, the frame chain (Moon principal-axis frame), and mission analy-

sis. The data are the Chebyshev coecients of the JPL DE440 development

verbatim ephemeris [45], copied

 never retted  from the JPL-distributed

kernels de440s.bsp (planets and Moon) and moon_pa_de440_200625.bpc

(lunar orientation) into the SREPH v1 container by the star data fetch

de440s pipeline (python/star_reacher/data_fetch.py; format specica-

tion in docs/formats/sreph_v1.md). The in-core evaluator is implemented

in cpp/src/ephemeris.cpp; because the coecients are verbatim, the con-

tainer and evaluator contribute only oating-point evaluation error and the

accuracy of every returned quantity is inherited from DE440 itself.

6.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Time argument. All epochs are TDB seconds since J2000 TDB (JD
2451545.0 TDB), carried as one binary64 value  the native epoch representation of the source kernels. Conversion from the simulator's

38

internal timescale (TAI, decision D-6) to TDB is the time-systems chapter's responsibility, not this model's.
2. Frames and centers. Position components are resolved along ICRF
axes, the inertial axes of DE440 [45]; the GCRF of Table 1.1 shares these axes. Each body is stored relative to its DE440 center: the solarsystem barycenter for the Sun, EMB, Venus, Mars, and Jupiter entries; the EMB for the Earth and Moon entries. The geocentric Moon state is composed at evaluation time as the dierence of the EMB-relative Moon and Earth states, so no coecient is retted.
3. Geometric states. Returned positions are instantaneous geomet-
ric states with no light-time or aberration correction, per the FR-23 light-time policy (dynamics use geometric ephemeris positions; optical sensor models apply their own corrections and bounds).
4. Lunar orientation. The libration output is the DE440 lunar principal-
axis orientation: the 3-1-3 Euler angles , ,  of the Moon principalaxis frame relative to the ICRF equator, with  accumulating without
wrapping, exactly as the source kernel stores it. Construction of the Moon PA rotation matrix from these angles belongs to the frames chapter.
Domain of validity: epochs within the records stored in the loaded le. The standard repack covers 2020-01-01 through 2060-01-01 TDB, widened outward to whole Chebyshev-record boundaries per body (records are never split); the loader accepts user-supplied wider trims (FR-4).
Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code: an epoch outside every
stored record of the queried body throws std::out_of_range naming the
body, the epoch, and the stored coverage; an unknown body name throws
std::invalid_argument listing the available bodies. The evaluator never
extrapolates a polynomial outside its record  Chebyshev extrapolation diverges rapidly and silently, so the guard is a hard error rather than a documented error growth.
Two accuracy boundaries inherited from the data are part of this domain statement. First, DE440 itself: its planetary and lunar trajectories carry the t uncertainties documented by Park et al. [45]; nothing in this simulator improves on them. Second, comparisons against ephemeris services that serve DE441  JPL Horizons among them  see the published DE440/DE441 lunar dierence: DE441 omits the lunar coremantle tidal damping term so it can span 30 000 years, and its lunar orbit consequently diers from DE440
39

by under 2 m across 19702020, growing to roughly 10 m per century away from the present, predominantly along-track [45]. The measured 1.85.4 m
dierence between this repack and DE441-sourced Horizons lunar states over 20202060 (Section 6.5) is that documented model dierence, not a repack error.

6.3 Derivation

6.3.1 Chebyshev representation of DE ephemerides

The JPL development ephemerides are distributed as piecewise Chebyshev
polynomial ts [44, 45]. Each body's trajectory is divided into contiguous
records (granules) of xed length L seconds; the DE440 values are L = 4 days
for the Moon and Earth (EMB-relative), 16 days for the Sun, EMB, and
Venus, 32 days for the Mars and Jupiter barycenters, and 8 days for the
lunar Euler angles. Within record k, beginning at epoch tk, each component p (a position coordinate in km, or an Euler angle in rad) is represented as

N -1
p(t) = cj Tj(x),
j=0

x = 2 (t - tk) - 1  [-1, 1], L

(6.1)

where Tj is the Chebyshev polynomial of the rst kind of degree j and N

is the per-segment coecient count (N  14 for every DE440 segment).

The coecients cj are produced by JPL's constrained least-squares t to the

and numerically integrated ephemeris; the t constrains position

velocity at

every record boundary, so the piecewise representation is continuous and dif-

ferentiable across records [44]. This constraint is what the record-boundary

continuity tests of Section 6.5 exercise.
Chebyshev polynomials satisfy Tj (cos ) = cos(j). With x = cos , the cosine addition identity cos((j+1)) + cos((j-1)) = 2 cos  cos(j) gives

the three-term recurrence

T0(x) = 1, T1(x) = x, Tj(x) = 2x Tj-1(x)-Tj-2(x), j  2. (6.2)

Dierentiating equation (6.2) with respect to x yields the companion recurrence for the derivatives Tj  dTj /dx:

T0(x) = 0,

T1(x) = 1,

Tj(x) = 2 Tj-1(x)+2x Tj-1(x)-Tj-2(x), j  2.

(6.3)

Both recurrences are numerically benign on x  [-1, 1], where |Tj (x)|  1.

The value and time derivative of the component follow by direct summation

This ascending-recurrence evaluation is the scheme used by JPL's own ephemeris interpolators for the same data [44].

6.3.2 Record selection

For a query epoch t inside a segment whose records begin at t0 with interval L, the evaluator selects record

k = t - t0 , L

clamped to k = n - 1 when t equals the segment end,

(6.5)

where n is the record count: a boundary epoch shared by records k - 1

begins and k belongs to the record that

there, and the nal epoch of the

segment evaluates in the last record at x = +1 exactly. Because the t

constrains both position and velocity at boundaries [44], either record yields

the same values to oating-point precision; the xed rule exists so that every

implementation selects the same record and reproduces bit-identical results

(D-10).

6.3.3 Units
SPK coecients are in km (positions) and PCK coecients in rad (angles) [41]; coecients are stored verbatim in those units, because rescaling them would round every coecient. Kind-0 outputs are converted to SI at
evaluation output by a single multiplication per component: rm = 1000 Ṗ rkm and vm/s = 1000 Ṗ vkm/s (the factor 1000 is exactly representable, so the
conversion costs one correctly rounded operation).

6.4 Discretization and implementation
1. Module and traceability. The evaluator lives in cpp/src/ephemeris.cpp;
the repack pipeline and the Python reference evaluator live in python/star_reacher/data_fetch. Both echo the labels eq:ephemeris:timescale, eq:ephemeris:recurrence, and eq:ephemeris:series verbatim at the corresponding code.

1.9Ṫ109 s lies in the binade [230, 231), so one ulp of the binary64 epoch is 230-52  2.4 Ṫ 10-7 s. At the fastest stored motion (Venus barycenter,  35 km s-1 about the SSB) an epoch rounded by half an ulp displaces the returned position by at most  8 mm  three orders below the 1 m
validation gate. The boundary-continuity measurements of Section 6.5
reproduce this number: the observed step across one epoch ulp at a
record boundary is the true motion over that interval.

6. No text parsing in the core. The SREPH container is a xed-
layout little-endian binary le (96-byte header, 64-byte directory entries, coecient blocks); the loader decodes it with xed-width reads and rejects malformed les  wrong magic, unsupported major version, truncated directory, or a coecient block running past end of le  with specic error messages (D-2 boundary rule; format specica-
tion in docs/formats/sreph_v1.md).

Chapter 7
Numerical Integrators
7.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the shared ordinary-dierential-equation integrator library (requirement FR-11): the xed-step classical fourth-order Runge Kutta method, the Fehlberg 7(8) embedded pair in both xed-step and adaptive modes, the per-state-group error norm and proportionalintegral (PI) step-size controller that drive the adaptive mode, and the cubic Hermite dense output that spans each accepted step. Every dynamical model in the simulator propagates through this library  models supply only their
right-hand side y = f (t, y)  so the accuracy, determinism, and step-control
behavior established here apply to the entire simulation. The dense output additionally feeds event location (Chapter 8) and uniform-rate logging. The
implementation lives in cpp/src/integrate.cpp.
7.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. The right-hand side f is suciently smooth on the span of each step: the classical convergence orders assume f  C 4 (RK4) and f  C 8
(the 7(8) pair) along the solution. Discontinuous dynamics  staging, impulsive maneuvers, frame re-centering  must be handled by stopping the integrator at the discontinuity through the event framework of Chapter 8 and restarting, never by stepping across it.
2. The problem is non-sti. Explicit RungeKutta methods have bounded stability regions; orbital and atmospheric-ight dynamics at the step
45

sizes used here sit well inside them.
3. The state is a at vector of doubles. Manifold-valued components (the unit quaternion of later phases) are integrated as raw components and repaired by the owning model (post-step normalization, FR-1); the integrator itself knows nothing of the constraint.
Domain of validity and out-of-domain behavior, matching the code:
 The adaptive mode's error control is asymptotic: it assumes the localerror expansion err  C h8 holds at the working step size. If the error test cannot be satised at the congured minimum step hmin 
the signature of stiness, a singularity, or an unreachable tolerance 
propagate throws std::runtime_error rather than silently delivering
an out-of-tolerance state.
 A step below the resolution of double precision at the current time (t + h = t in oating point) throws rather than looping forever.
 The dense output is third-order accurate regardless of the integrator
order (Section 7.3); consumers that need better interpolation accu-
racy must cap the step size (hmax), not tighten the integrator tol-
erance. This is the documented control for microsecond-level event timing (Chapter 8).
 Tolerances are per state group with di > 0 enforced; a group par-
tition that does not exactly cover the state vector is rejected with
std::invalid_argument.

7.3 Derivation

7.3.5 PI step-size control
In the asymptotic regime the error estimate obeys errn  Cnhkn with k = 8 (the order of the embedded estimate, equation (7.7)). The elementary controller inverts this relation toward err = 1: hn+1 = S hn err-n 1/k with safety factor S < 1. Gustafsson's control-theoretic analysis [19] showed that this pure-integral rule oscillates when Cn drifts along the trajectory, and that
adding a proportional term on the error history damps it. The resulting PI
controller, in the form given by Hairer and Wanner [21], Section IV.2, is

hn+1 = hn Ṗ clamp S errn-1 errn-2 1, fmin, fmax ,

0.7

0.4

1 =

, k

2 =

, k

(7.9)

with the exponent pair recommended there (kI = 0.3/k, kP = 0.4/k in integral/proportional form; 1 = kI + kP , 2 = kP ). The implementation uses S = 0.9, growth/shrink clamps fmin = 0.2, fmax = 5, and three standard safeguards from the same sources: the error history is seeded with err-1 = 1

so the rst step reduces to the elementary controller; the step never grows

on the rst acceptance after a rejection; and rejected steps are re-proposed

with the elementary controller clamped to no growth. Steps are clamped to
[hmin, hmax] throughout.

49

7.3.6 Cubic Hermite dense output
Each accepted step already holds the endpoint states y0 = y(t0), y1 = y(t0 + h) and derivatives f0, f1, which determine a unique cubic (Hermite) interpolant. With  = (t - t0)/h  [0, 1],

u() = (1-) y0+ y1+(-1) (1-2)(y1-y0)+(-1) hf0+ hf1 , (7.10)

which satises u(0) = y0, u(1) = y1, u(0) = hf0, and u(1) = hf1 by direct
evaluation of the polynomial and its derivative; this is the standard order-3
dense output of RungeKutta theory [20].
Interpolation error. Let y  C4[t0, t1] be a scalar solution component
with Hermite interpolant H matching y and y at both endpoints, and x t  (t0, t1). Dene (s) = (s - t0)2(s - t1)2 and the auxiliary function w(s) = y(s) - H(s) - K (s) with K chosen so that w(t) = 0. Then w has
ve zeros in [t0, t1] counted with multiplicity (double zeros at t0 and t1, a simple zero at t), so by repeated application of Rolle's theorem w(4) has a zero   (t0, t1). Since H is cubic, H (4) = 0, and (4) = 4! = 24, whence 0 = y(4)() - 24K and

consequences drive design decisions elsewhere:

 The interpolant is lower order than both integrators (O(h4) against
O(h5) local for RK4 and O(h9) local for the extrapolated 7(8) pair),
so any quantity read o the dense output  interpolated log records,
located event times  is interpolant-limited and improves as h4 only. Capping hmax is the documented control (Chapter 8 derives the result-
ing event-timing error law).

 The bound assumes exact endpoint data; the integrator's own local
error adds a term of the integrator's order, negligible for the 7(8) pair
at the step sizes where the h4 term matters.

7.4 Discretization and implementation
1. Module and traceability. The library lives in cpp/src/integrate.cpp
with the public interface in cpp/include/star/integrate.hpp. The

50

source comments echo the labels eq:integrators:rk4, eq:integrators:rkf78:stages, eq:integrators:rkf78:err, eq:integrators:errnorm, eq:integrators:pi, and eq:integrators:hermite verbatim at the corresponding code.
2. Right-hand-side interface. Models supply f (t, y) through a non-
owning function reference (integrate::RhsRef): one indirect call per
evaluation, no allocation, no virtual dispatch, storage-agnostic rawpointer signature. This is the permanent hot-loop interface.
3. Determinism (D-10). Stage evaluations and the weighted combi-
nations of equations (7.5) and (7.6) run in xed ascending order; the tableau's zero entries are skipped by a compile-time-constant pattern, so the oating-point operation sequence is identical across runs and platforms. All workspace is allocated at construction; the step loop
performs no heap allocation. The test rkf78_adaptive_double_run_bitwise
gates bitwise equality of two identical adaptive runs, controller history included.
4. Local extrapolation. Rkf78::step writes the eighth-order solution
and returns the embedded dierence of equation (7.7) as the error
vector; the controller's order constant is accordingly k = 8.
5. Terminal step. The driver truncates the nal step to land exactly
on the requested end time; a truncated step is integrated with the
truncated h, not interpolated.
6. Zero error estimate. err = 0 (dynamics the pair integrates exactly)
grows the step at fmax instead of dividing by zero, and the stored error
history is oored at a tiny positive value.
7. Convergence-measurement design. The validation measurements
end below use a dyadic span (t = 7168 s = 210 Ṗ 7) and power-of-two step
sizes, so every step time k h is exactly representable and accumulated
time carries zero rounding error. The ladders keep the smallest trunca-
tion errorat least 2.5 orders of magnitude above the position roundo oor ( N ulp(|r|)  6 Ṫ 10-8 m here), which is how the measured
slopes avoid the double-precision plateau. The choices are recorded
with the measured errors in cpp/tests/test_integrate.cpp.

Chapter 8
Event Detection
8.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the event-detection framework (requirement FR-
12): scalar event functions g(t, y) screened for sign changes on every accepted
integrator step, root location by Brent's method on the step's dense output
to a congurable time tolerance (1 Ṫ 10-9 s by default), direction lters, and
integrator restart at the located root with an optional discrete state update. This is the mechanism by which the mission sequence acts on the trajectory: the Phase 2 event set is timers and apsis crossings, and later phases add staging, ignition/cuto, sphere-of-inuence transitions, node crossings, and ground impact as additional event functions  the framework itself does
not change. The implementation lives in cpp/src/events.cpp, on top of
the integrators and dense output of Chapter 7.
8.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Each event function g(t, y) is continuous in t along the trajectory within a step, and dierentiable at its roots with g (t) = 0 (simple
crossings). Brent's method still converges on roots of odd multiplicity (bisection fallback), but the timing-error analysis below assumes simple roots.
2. Event functions are computable from (t, y) alone  no history, no side
eects. Discrete behavior belongs in the update hook, which runs only at located roots.
54

3. At most one sign change of each event function occurs per accepted step. Sign screening is blind to an even number of crossings inside one step (the endpoint signs match); the mitigation is capping the step
length hmax below half the shortest oscillation period of any registered
event function.

Domain of validity and out-of-domain behavior, matching the code:

 Located event times inherit the dense-output interpolation error (equa-

tion (8.3)); the framework honors its 1 Ṫ 10-9 s root tolerance with

interpolated respect to the

event function. Consumers needing a spe-

cic accuracy against the true trajectory must budget the h4 term via

hmax, as the apsis validation case does.

 The apsis event function (equation (8.5)) degenerates as e  0: on a circular orbit g = r Ṗ v is identically zero and apsides are undened. The framework itself is unaected (a g that stays at zero never screens
as a crossing, by the strict-sign rule of equation (8.1)); the event simply
reports nothing, which is the correct degenerate answer.

 An event whose g is exactly zero at the propagation start (or at a restart) is not red until g leaves zero: screening requires a strictly
signed starting value.

 Roots of the same event closer together than the time tolerance are
indistinguishable by construction and re once.

8.3 Derivation

8.3.1 Sign screening with direction lters

Let g0 = g(t0, y0) and g1 = g(t1, y1) be the event function at the endpoints of an accepted step. A crossing is agged in (t0, t1] when

g0 < 0  g1  0 or g0 > 0  g1  0,

(8.1)

increasing

decreasing

ltered by the event's direction setting (increasing only, decreasing only, or either). By the intermediate value theorem the continuous interpolated event function of equation (8.2) then has at least one root in the step.

55

8.3.2 Root location on the dense output

Evaluating g on the true solution inside a step is not possible without further

interpolated integration; the framework instead locates roots of the

event

function

g^( ) = g , u( ) ,   [t0, t1],

(8.2)

where u is the cubic Hermite dense output of equation (7.10). Because u reproduces the step endpoints exactly, g^ carries the already-computed endpoint values g0, g1, and the screened bracket transfers verbatim.
The root is located with Brent's method [7]: the guaranteed-convergent
combination of bisection, the secant rule, and inverse quadratic interpola-
tion, taking the interpolation step only when it falls safely inside the current
bracket and shrinks faster than the previous-but-one step, and bisecting oth-
erwise. Brent proves (i) convergence is never worse than a bounded multiple
of bisection  at most O log22((b - a)/) function evaluations for bracket [a, b] and tolerance   and (ii) on simple roots of smooth functions conver-
gence is superlinear [7]. The implementation iterates until the bracket width
is within  = t + 4  |t|, honoring the congured tolerance t down to the
resolution of double precision at the root's magnitude.

8.3.3 Event-timing error law
The located time t^ is a root of g^, not of the true g( ) = g(, y( )). For a simple root at t, expanding g about t and bounding |g^ - g|  Lg u - y
with the Hermite bound of equation (7.11) gives

t^- t



Lg |g (t )|

h4 384

max

y(4)

+ t,

(8.3)

where Lg is the Lipschitz constant of g in y on the step and t the root tolerance. Event timing therefore improves as h4 and is controlled by hmax,
exactly as anticipated in Chapter 7. For the apsis validation case below
(hmax = 5 s on the reference orbit), the h4 term evaluates to  5 Ṫ 10-11 s, so the located times are dominated by the 1 Ṫ 10-9 s root tolerance  three
orders inside the 1 ṁs acceptance gate, and consistent with the measured 3.4 Ṫ 10-4 ṁs worst case.

8.3.4 Restart with discrete update
Reading the event-time state o the dense output would inject the full O(h4) interpolation error into the trajectory. Instead, after locating t^ the driver

56

re-integrates the step from t0 with step length t^ - t0, so the state deliv-
ered at the event carries integrator accuracy; the shortened step needs no

error re-test because it is interior to a step that already passed. The event's

discrete update hook may then modify the state in place (mass drop, impul-

sive maneuver, origin re-centering in later phases), propagation restarts from
(t^, y(t^)), and all event functions are re-evaluated there. Terminal events stop propagation at t^ instead.

Two safeguards make restart robust at the root. First, the driver res at

post-crossing the bracket endpoint on the

side of the root (both endpoints are

within the tolerance), so integration resumes with the sign change already

behind it. Second, for events without a discrete update the stored screening

sign is forced to the crossed side, so interpolant-level noise around zero cannot

re-re the event; when an update ran, the re-evaluated value stands, because
the hook may legitimately move g (re-arming a timer, changing regime).

8.3.5 Phase 2 event functions

Timer. An event at xed time te uses

g(t, y) = t - te,

(8.4)

linear in t and independent of the state, so equation (8.3) reduces to the root tolerance alone (Lg = 0): timers isolate the root-nding and restart
machinery in validation.
Apsis crossing. For a translational state [r, v] about a central body,
apsides are the extrema of r = r, i.e. the zeros of r r = r Ṗ v:

g(t, y) = r Ṗ v.

(8.5)

Under two-body dynamics (equation (2.4)), g = v Ṗ v + r Ṗ v = v2 - ṁ/r. Evaluating on the ellipse with semi-latus rectum p = a(1 - e2) (Vallado [57]): at periapsis vp2 = (ṁ/p)(1+e)2 and ṁ/rp = (ṁ/p)(1+e), so gp = ṁe(1+e)/p > 0; at apoapsis ga = -ṁe(1 - e)/p < 0. Periapsis is therefore an increasing crossing of g and apoapsis a decreasing one, which is how the two direction-
ltered event registrations in the validation suite distinguish them, and |g | at the roots   8.8 Ṫ 106 m2/s3 for the reference orbit  is the denominator
in equation (8.3).

8.4 Discretization and implementation
1. Module and traceability. The framework lives in cpp/src/events.cpp
with the public interface in cpp/include/star/events.hpp. Source

57

comments echo the labels eq:events:screen and eq:events:ghat at the screening and root-location code, and eq:events:timer and eq:events:apsis at the two event functions.
2. Extension contract. An event type is a callable g(t, y) plus a direc-
tion, an optional update hook, and a terminal ag (EventSpec); Phase
3+ event types plug in without framework changes. All framework references to user code are non-owning function references, matching the integrator's hot-loop interface.
3. Determinism (D-10). Events are screened in registration order every
step; when several events root within the same step the earliest located time res, with exact ties resolved to the lowest index. Brent's iteration is pure double arithmetic on the bracket; all workspace is pre-allocated. The only allocation after setup is the growth of the caller-supplied event log when an event actually res (callers may reserve).
4. Bracket endpoints for free. Because the dense output reproduces
step endpoints bitwise, the screening values g0, g1 seed Brent's bracket without re-evaluation, and g1 of an accepted step is reused as g0 of the
next.
5. Tolerance oor. The root tolerance degrades gracefully to 4|t| when
the congured t is below the resolution of double at the root's mag-
nitude.

Table 8.1 lists the tests that constitute this chapter's validation evidence.
Each identier is machine-checked to exist in the test tree by scripts/lint_chapters.py; the analytic apsis times are committed goldens with provenance (tests/golden/integrators/manifest and the apsis measurement is reproduced from Python by tests/python/test_integrators.py.

Chapter 9
Spherical-Harmonic Gravity
9.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the harmonic gravity model (FR-5): evaluation of the gravitational acceleration of an extended central body from a fully normalized spherical-harmonic coecient set  Earth EGM2008, Moon GRGM1200A, Mars MRO120F  in the body-xed frame, using the Pines formulation, which is regular at the poles. The model supports a runtime truncation degree and order and the three FR-5 delity tiers (point-
mass, J2-only, full n Ṫ m). Field data arrives either from in-memory arrays (tests) or from the SRGRAV v1 binary container written by star data fetch (docs/formats/srgrav_v1.md); the returned acceleration al-
ways includes the central (degree-0) term. The module is implemented in
cpp/src/models/gravity.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/gravity.hpp;
body-frame orientation is the frames chapter's responsibility (Chapter 5).
9.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Static, rigid eld. The coecient set is constant: solid and ocean
tides, atmospheric loading, and secular CŸ2,0 drift are unmodeled. Their eect on the low-degree coecients is at the 10-810-9 level of CŸ2,0 [46],
far below the mission-analysis delity this simulator targets.
2. Fully normalized inputs. Coecients are 4 (geodesy) fully nor-
malized CŸnm, SŸnm; the data pipeline rejects any source that declares another normalization. Each eld's ṁ = GM and reference radius R
60

come from the same source header as its coecients  the triple is
self-consistent and is never mixed with constants from elsewhere. In
particular EGM2008's ṁ = 3.986 004 415 Ṫ 1014 m3 s-2 diers deliberately from the IERS value in constants.hpp [47] used by the two-body
placeholder model.

3. Permanent-tide convention documented, not applied. The tide
system of each source (EGM2008 tide-free per its header; MRO120F
tide-free per its PDS label; GRGM1200A not stated by its label, recorded
as unknown) is carried through the SRGRAV header for cross-tool
bookkeeping. It never enters evaluation; it only aects which CŸ2,0
convention a comparison tool must be fed.

4. Exterior evaluation. The exterior series converges for r greater than
the Brillouin sphere radius (here the reference radius R); all validation states satisfy r > R. Below R the series may diverge and results are
not trustworthy.

5. Body-xed input, body-xed output. Position and acceleration
are resolved in the source model's body-xed frame (ITRS-aligned for EGM2008, lunar principal axes for GRGM1200A, IAU Mars body-xed for MRO120F). Rotation into the integration frame is composed from Chapter 5 and is outside this module.

Domain of validity: degrees up to the shipped maxima (70 Ṫ 70 Earth, 120 Ṫ 120 Moon, 80 Ṫ 80 Mars; FR-5). The normalized recursions of Sec-

tion 9.3 are the forward-stable column recursions recommended for nonsingu-
lar geopotential models [34]; the normalized Helmholtz values AŸnm(u) grow to at most  1023 near |u| = 1 at degree 120 while their multipliers rm, im decay as cosm , so every summed term is bounded by the corresponding normalized-Legendre magnitude O( 2n + 1) and binary64 overow is ex-

cluded by orders of magnitude at the shipped degrees.

Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: a requested trunca-
tion degree or order beyond the stored band throws std::invalid_argument

(the le carries no information above its band; delity is never silently de-
graded); evaluation at r = 0 throws std::domain_error; the J2-only tier on a eld of degree < 2 throws std::invalid_argument; a malformed SRGRAV

le (magic, major version, size, tide code) is rejected by the loader with

surface std::runtime_error naming the defect. Evaluation at R

<r<R

(possible for the Moon and Mars, whose reference radii exceed parts of the

physical surface) proceeds without warning; assumption 4 bounds its trust-

worthiness.

9.4 Discretization and implementation
1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/gravity.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:gravity:potential, eq:gravity:pines, eq:gravity:diag, eq:gravity:subdiag, eq:gravity:column, eq:gravity:deriv, eq:gravity:rmim, eq:gravity:sums, and eq:gravity:accel verba-
tim.
2. Precomputed recursion tables; no per-call allocation. The
square-root coecients of equations (9.7)(9.10) depend only on (n, m);
the evaluator computes them once at construction for the eld's full de-
gree, together with all workspace (AŸ triangle, rm/im, n). The per-call
path is multiplyadd only and allocation-free (D-10: no heap allocation in the propagation loop).
3. Fixed evaluation order (D-10). Per call: the AŸ triangle is lled
diagonal rst, then rst sub-diagonal, then column by column in as-
cending n for each m (the forward-stable direction [34]); the four sums of equation (9.12) accumulate in ascending n outer, ascending m inner order. The full triangle (m  n) is computed regardless of the order truncation because equation (9.10) reads column m + 1.
4. Tiers and truncation. The FR-5 tiers are loop bounds: point-mass
evaluates n = 0 only; J2-only evaluates n  {0, 2}, m = 0 (skipping n = 1 so a hypothetical non-zero stored degree-1 row cannot leak into the tier); full nṪm evaluates the requested band, which must lie within
the stored band (out-of-band requests throw; Section 9.2). Runtime truncation is arithmetically identical to load-time truncation  the
same terms in the same order  which gravity_truncation_consistency
pins at bit level.
5. Pole behavior and underow. At |u|  1 the AŸnm grow while
rm, im  cosm  decay; products remain bounded (Section 9.2). Within  10-2 degrees of a pole, high-order rm, im underow gradually to zero; the aected terms are below 10-300 of the total and IEEE-754 gradual
underow (guaranteed by the D-10 ags) keeps the result deterministic.
6. SRGRAV loader. Binary read only (D-2): magic and major version
checked rst, then degree/order plausibility, tide-system code, and an exact le-size-versus-header check before any coecient is interpreted;
failures name the defect. Coecients, ṁ, and R are stored and con-
sumed as one indivisible model (assumption 2).
65

7. Data pipeline. star data fetch egm2008 | grgm1200a | mro120f
downloads each pinned source (SHA-256), parses the ICGEM gfc or PDS SHADR text in Python (D-2 boundary), truncates to the FR5 degrees, and writes SRGRAV; the committed test excerpts under
tests/golden/gravity/ carry the same data in CSV and SRGRAV
form with byte-anchored equality between the two (provenance: that
directory's manifest.toml). 9.5 Validation evidence
Table 9.1 lists the tests that constitute this chapter's validation evidence.
Each test identier is machine-checked to exist in the test tree by scripts/lint_chapters.py; golden provenance and tolerances are recorded in tests/golden/gravity/manifest.toml. 9.6 References

Chapter 10
Third-Body Gravitational Perturbation
10.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the third-body gravitational perturbation model (FR-6): the dierential acceleration a spacecraft experiences, relative to its central body, from the point-mass gravity of an additional attracting body (Sun, Moon, Venus, Jupiter, or Earth, per the FR-6 regime rules), evaluated
in the cancellation-safe f (q) formulation of Battin [5]. The naive dierence of
two nearly equal acceleration vectors loses a geometry-dependent number of
signicant digits in double precision; the f (q) reformulation is algebraically
identical but avoids the catastrophic subtraction, which is what Phase 3 exit
criterion 7 gates. The model is implemented in cpp/src/models/thirdbody.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/thirdbody.hpp; third-body
positions come from the ephemeris evaluator of Chapter 6, and gravitational parameters are supplied by the caller (the model hardcodes no body data).
10.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Point-mass third body. The perturbing body is a point mass or,
by Newton's shell theorem, a spherically symmetric mass distribution;
its eld is characterized entirely by ṁ3 = GM3. Third-body harmonic
structure (indirect oblateness) is a PRD non-goal.
68

2. Test-particle spacecraft. The spacecraft's mass is negligible: it
perturbs neither the central nor the third body.
3. Common frame, common origin. Both input vectors  the space-
craft position r and the third-body position s  are resolved in the
same GCRF-oriented inertial frame and are both relative to the central body's center. The model is purely algebraic in these inputs; frame bookkeeping is the caller's responsibility.
4. Geometric ephemeris positions. s is the geometric (instantaneous)
position from Chapter 6; light-time and aberration corrections are excluded from dynamics by the PRD light-time policy (FR-23). The
neglected retardation displaces the Sun by  500 s Ṫ 30 km s-1  1.5 Ṫ 107 m, i.e.  10-4 of s, changing the perturbing acceleration
by the same relative order  the standard convention for planetary force models.
Domain of validity: any geometry with r = s and s = 0, for every
body pair of the FR-6 set; the formulation is exact for all separation ratios
(it is not a series expansion), so cislunar geometries with r  s are as valid as LEOSun geometries with r  s. The oating-point error bound of Section 10.4 additionally assumes r < s (spacecraft inside the
third body's distance), which regime validation (FR-15) guarantees for every congurable case.
Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: at r = s the denominator 3 vanishes and the model returns non-nite values (division by zero propagates IEEE innities or NaNs); at s = 0 likewise. No function of
this module throws: it runs inside the deterministic time loop, and excluding physically impossible states (a spacecraft coincident with a body center) is the conguration validator's job, not the hot path's.

10.3 Derivation

10.3.2 Why the naive form cancels
For r  s, expand equation (10.3) to rst order in r/s (the tidal limit): p  (ṁ3/s3) 3(r Ṗ s^)s^ - r , whose magnitude lies between ṁ3r/s3 (for r  s) and 2ṁ3r/s3 (for r  s). Each of the two terms in equation (10.3) has magnitude  ṁ3/s2, so the subtraction cancels all but a fraction  r/s of the operands: with operand rounding at relative   1.1 Ṫ 10-16, the dierence carries a relative error of order  s/r. For the classic LEOSun geometry (r  6.8 Ṫ 106 m, s  1.5 Ṫ 1011 m) that is a loss of roughly
four to six signicant digits depending on rounding luck; the committed
near-alignment golden state (a low lunar orbiter with Jupiter at a far con-
junction, s/r  5.4 Ṫ 105) demonstrates a measured loss of 6.1 digits (test thirdbody_naive_cancellation_digit_loss).

The reformulation is safe because no step forms a small dierence of large

The observed generation-time error of the double-precision f (q) evaluation against the extended-precision reference is at most 3.4 Ṫ 10-16 over the ten

10.4 Discretization and implementation
There is no discretization: the model is a pointwise algebraic map from
(ṁ3, r, s) to p, evaluated inside the force composition at whatever states the
integrator (Chapter 7) requests. Implementation notes:
1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/thirdbody.cpp.
The source comments echo the labels eq:thirdbody:q, eq:thirdbody:fq, and eq:thirdbody:accel verbatim; the test's naive reference evaluation echoes eq:thirdbody:naive.
2. No per-call allocation. All intermediates are xed-size Eigen vec-
tors and scalars on the stack; the function allocates nothing, per the deterministic-loop rules.
3. Fixed evaluation order, basic operations only. The implemen-
tation uses only IEEE-754 basic operations (+, -, Ṫ, ṫ, sqrt), all cor-
rectly rounded, in a xed order compiled without contraction (D-10). The golden generator's Python mirror reproduces the same operation sequence statement for statement, so its generation-time error measurements transfer bit-exactly to every CI platform.
4. The naive form never ships. Equation (10.3) is evaluated in double
precision only inside the validation test, to demonstrate the digit loss the formulation exists to avoid.
5. Data ownership. ṁ3 values are supplied by the caller (DE440 header
values wired in by the force-composition layer); the module denes no body constants.

Chapter 11
Solar Radiation Pressure and Conical Shadow
11.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the solar-radiation-pressure model (FR-7): the attitudeindependent cannonball acceleration with ephemeris Sun distance, scaled by
an illumination fraction   [0, 1] from a dual-cone (umbra/penumbra) coni-
cal shadow model that any congured spherical body  including the current central body  may cast. The shadow function is a separately callable, separately testable component: besides scaling the SRP force it supplies the signed boundary functions that the event-detection framework of Chapter 8 screens for eclipse-entry and -exit events (FR-12). The model is implemented
in cpp/src/models/srp.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/srp.hpp;
Sun and occulter positions come from the ephemeris evaluator of Chapter 6,
and all body radii and the spacecraft ballistic parameter CRA/m are supplied
by the caller.
11.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Cannonball spacecraft. The SRP force is attitude-independent,
characterized by the single lumped parameter CRA/m: an eective cross-section A, mass m, and radiation pressure coecient CR that absorbs the absorbed/reected momentum accounting (CR = 1 for a perfect absorber, up to 2 for a at specular reector facing the Sun; a
75

sphere

with

diuse

reectivity



has

CR

=

1

+

4 9

,

Montenbruck

and

Gill [38], Sec. 3.4). The N-plate upgrade path of FR-7 replaces this

parameterization without touching the shadow model.

2. Inverse-square ux from the nominal irradiance. The solar ux
is (d) = 1 au(au/d)2 with the IAU 2015 Resolution B3 nominal total solar irradiance 1 au = 1361 W m-2 (PrĠa et al. [49]). The measured solar-cycle TSI variation is  1.6 W m-2 peak-to-peak ( 0.12%) about a minimum of 1360.8(5) W m-2 (Kopp and Lean [31]); using the con-
stant nominal bounds the SRP force error at the same relative level,
far below the uncertainty of any congured CR.

3. Geometric Sun position. As in Chapter 10, the Sun position is
geometric (FR-23 light-time policy). Light-time and aberration dis-
place the apparent Sun by  10-4 of its distance, a direction error of  10-4 rad and a ux error of  10-4 relative  both absorbed by the CR uncertainty.

4. Spherical, opaque, airless occulters. Each occulting body is a
sphere of caller-supplied radius. Neglected against the Earth case:
oblateness (the  1/298 attening perturbs the shadow-boundary radius by up to  21 km, shifting LEO crossing times by up to a few sec-
onds depending on crossing geometry) and atmospheric refraction/extinction (which softens the real penumbra by an altitude-dependent amount). These are physical-delity bounds of the model, not of its implementation; the Phase 3 criterion gates the implementation against the model's own exact geometry.

5. Uniform solar disk. Solar limb darkening is neglected: the penum-

area bra illumination fraction is the uncovered

fraction of a uniformly

bright disk (the standard model, Montenbruck and Gill [38], Sec. 3.4).

6. Flat-disk overlap in the penumbra interior. The umbra/penumbra/annular

boundaries follow from exact sphere tangency (Section 11.3); only the

interior partial-phase

value of  treats the two apparent disks as pla-

nar circles of radii equal to their angular radii. For a LEO spacecraft
eclipsed by the Earth the occulter's angular radius ( 1.2 rad) is large, but the solar disk ( 4.7 Ṫ 10-3 rad) sees the occulter limb as locally straight to  as/ tan ao  0.3%; the induced  error is below 10-2 of the penumbra transition, which lasts seconds and carries  10-7 m/s2

of acceleration  negligible against assumption 4.

76

Domain of validity: spacecraft outside both spheres (r - r > R, ro - r > Ro), any occulter/Sun geometry including the annular case (ao < as), occulters at any distance. Multiple occulting bodies are composed by the force-assembly layer (evaluating  per occulter); this chapter denes the
single-occulter function.
Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: if the spacecraft
is inside an occulting sphere, the arcsin argument is clamped to 1 (ao = /2) and the function still returns a well-dened value continuous with the
exterior; sub-surface states are excluded by ground-impact eventing (FR-12),
so no throw is warranted in the hot loop. If the spacecraft coincides with
the Sun's center the direction s^ is undened and IEEE NaNs propagate.  is exactly 1 in full sunlight and exactly 0 in total umbra by construction
(returned as literal constants, not computed expressions).

11.3 Derivation

11.3.1 Radiation pressure and the cannonball acceleration

11.3.3 Signed boundary functions for event detection

The event framework (Chapter 8) screens scalar functions for sign changes, so the two shadow boundaries are exposed directly:

(11.8)

itself, which is constant outside the penumbra and therefore useless for sign
screening.

11.4 Discretization and implementation

There is no discretization: both functions are pointwise algebraic maps evaluated at integrator-requested states. Implementation notes:

1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/srp.cpp;
source comments echo eq:srp:pressure, eq:srp:cannonball, eq:srp:appgeom, eq:srp:overlap, eq:srp:nu, and eq:srp:boundaries verbatim. The
analytic cone reference (equations (11.9), (11.10), (11.11)) is imple-
mented only in cpp/tests/test_srp.cpp, echoed there, so the vali-
dation reference cannot share a defect with the model.

2. Shared apparent geometry. One internal helper computes (as, ao, )
for the fraction and both boundary functions, so the three public functions cannot disagree about the geometry.

3. Angle numerics.  is evaluated as atan2(u Ṫ v , u Ṗ v), which is
accurate for all separations, unlike arccos of the normalized dot product, which loses precision near 0 and   and eclipse geometry lives near   ao, which for LEO is O(1) but must resolve O(as) differences. arcsin arguments are clamped to [0, 1] (out-of-domain rule above); arccos arguments in equation (11.6) are clamped to [-1, 1] and the chord height uses max(0, Ṗ), protecting boundary-adjacent
states from sub-ulp excursions outside the real domain.

Exact 0 and 1. 4.

The full-sunlight and total-umbra branches return

the literals 1.0 and 0.0 before any area arithmetic runs, so  is bit-exact

in both regimes  the property the determinism gates and the force-

by-source log channels rely on. The umbra case of the acceleration is
exactly zero because  = 0 multiplies the nite coecient.

5. Conditioning of the partial branch. In equation (11.6) the occulter-
disk term a2o arccos ( - xc)/ao evaluates its arccos near argument 1
when the occulter disk is much larger than the solar disk (LEO Earth
shadow: ao  1.2 rad vs. as  4.7 Ṫ 10-3 rad), amplifying ulp-level

81

angle errors by a2o/ a2s 1 - (( - xc)/ao)2  106107 after the a2s normalization. The double-precision partial-phase  therefore carries an absolute error of order 10-9 at such geometries (observed worst 1.0 Ṫ 10-9 at the committed penumbra states), while small-occulter partial and annular geometries stay at 10-12. This is retained deliberately: the formula is the cited standard, the error is  10-9 of the SRP force during a seconds-long transit  far below the CR knowledge of
assumption 1 and the physical delity bounds of assumptions 46 
and the regime boundaries and exact 0/1 branches are unaected. The golden tolerance (1 Ṫ 10-8 absolute on partial values) encodes exactly
this bound.
6. Constants. c, au, 1 au, P1 au = 1 au/c (a compile-time quotient of
the two cited constants), and R live in cpp/include/star/constants.hpp,
each cited at its denition. Occulter radii are caller-supplied (test geometry uses representative Earth/Moon values; physical values are wired by the force-composition layer with the rest of the body data).
7. Determinism. No per-call allocation; xed evaluation order. The
libm calls (arcsin, arccos, atan2) are the only non-correctly-rounded
operations and thus the cross-platform divergence surface (D-10); the
golden tolerances (tests/golden/srp/manifest.toml) budget for their
few-ulp spread.
