Chapter 12
Earth Atmosphere: U.S. Standard Atmosphere 1976
12.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the Earth launch atmosphere (FR-8): the U.S. Stan-
dard Atmosphere, 1976 (USSA76) [43]. Below 86 km the model is fully ana-
lytic from the document's dening constants and returns temperature, pressure, density, and speed of sound  the quantities the Phase 4 aerodynamics model needs for Mach number and dynamic pressure and the propulsion
model needs for back-pressure thrust. From 86 km to 1000 km the model
returns density only, by documented interpolation of the published USSA76 tables; this extension exists for prole continuity (launch aerodynamics live
below 86 km, and orbit-decay drag uses the HarrisPriester model of Chapter 13). The model is implemented in cpp/src/models/atmosphere_ussa76.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/atmosphere_ussa76.hpp.
12.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Standard static atmosphere. USSA76 is an idealized, steady-state,
mid-latitude annual-mean prole [43]. There is no dependence on season, latitude, local time, or space weather; day-to-day density at altitude can dier from the standard by large factors. The model is the conventional reference for launch aerodynamics, not a weather model.
2. Molecular-scale temperature identication below 86 km. The
84

model computes and returns the molecular-scale temperature TM of equation (12.3). The document denes the kinetic temperature T = TM Ṗ M/M0 with a molecular-weight ratio that departs from unity only between 80 and 86 km, by at most 0.04 %, and its own main tables print T = TM throughout that band (the correction is left to the user; [43,
Part 1, 1.2.4, p. 9]). This model adopts the same tabulation practice, so its temperature reproduces the printed Table I values exactly and
is at most 0.04 % above the rigorously corrected kinetic temperature between 80 and 86 km. Pressure and density are unaected (both are dened in terms of TM ).
3. Constant sea-level composition below 86 km (M0 = 28.9644 kg kmol-1),
per the document's mixing assumption [43, Part 1, 1.2.4].
4. Tabulated densities above 86 km. The document computes pres-
sure and density above 86 km from species number-density integrals
(diusion equations for N2, O, O2, Ar, He, H; [43, Part 1, 1.3.1, eq. 33c]). Those integrals are deliberately out of scope here: the model instead interpolates the published Table I densities on a committed
node grid (equation (12.8)). Only density is provided above 86 km;
temperature, pressure, and speed of sound are not (the printed speed-
of-sound tables themselves terminate at 86 km [43, Part 1, 1.3.10]).
Domain of validity: geometric altitude z  [-5 km, 86 km) for the full analytic state (the table's own lower limit is -5 km); z  [86 km, 1000 km] for
density only. One boundary subtlety is adopted deliberately: the document
equates the top of the seventh geopotential layer, H7 = 84852 m, with 86 km geometric, but the exact conversion of z = 86 000 m gives H = 84852.046 m
 the stated equivalence is a rounded convention. The implementation
branches on geometric altitude at exactly 86 km and lets the layer-7 formulas extend approximately 5 cm of geopotential past H7, so the analytic and
tabulated regions meet without a gap. The resulting seam discrepancy is
print rounding only, measured at 2.6 Ṫ 10-5 relative and gated at 2 Ṫ 10-4 by ATM-USSA76-CONTINUITY.
Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: altitudes below
-5 km or above 1000 km, and non-nite inputs, throw std::domain_error; requesting the full thermodynamic state at or above 86 km also throws std::domain_error (the quantities do not exist in this model there, and
returning a fabricated value would violate the no-silent-default rule, DX-2).
The guard is gated by ATM-USSA76-DOMAIN.
85

12.3 Derivation

1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/atmosphere_ussa76.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:ussa76:geopotential, eq:ussa76:hydro, eq:ussa76:tm, eq:ussa76:gradient, eq:ussa76:isothermal, eq:ussa76:density, eq:ussa76:speedofsound, and eq:ussa76:interp verbatim.

87

to this model, and cited at their denitions in the source. They are

not deliberately

promoted to star/constants.hpp: they dene this

document's atmosphere, not the project's physical-constant set.

3. Fixed-order layer walk. Layer base values (TM,b, Pb) are computed
once, in xed order b = 0..6, and cached in a function-local static;
every subsequent evaluation walks the same xed sequence (D-10: xed
evaluation order, single-threaded core).

4. Branch at exactly 86 km. z < 86 000 m selects the analytic branch
(layer-7 formulas extended  5 cm of geopotential past H7, per Section 12.2); z  86 000 m selects the node-grid branch, whose rst node is exactly 86 000 m.

5. Compiled-in node table with a committed check copy. The
node grid is compiled into the model source, and tests/golden/atmosphere/ussa76_upper_nodes
carries the same values as an independently reviewable transcription
check; test ATM-USSA76-UPPER-NODES requires the two copies to agree bit-for-bit after strtod. A runtime le load was rejected: the core
never parses text (D-2).

Determinism. 6.

All paths are straight-line binary64 arithmetic in xed

order under the D-10 ags. The gradient-layer power in equation (12.4)
and the exponentials use libm pow/exp/log, so cross-platform results

may dier in the last ulp; all committed tolerances sit orders of mag-

nitude above that spread.

Chapter 13
Earth Atmosphere: HarrisPriester Density Model
13.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the orbit-decay drag atmosphere (FR-8): the modied HarrisPriester density model in the form given by Montenbruck and Gill [38, Sect. 3.5.2], whose underlying physics is the time-dependent upperatmosphere model of Harris and Priester [22]. The model is fully deterministic  a xed mean-solar-activity coecient table plus a diurnal-bulge term, with no space-weather inputs (D-10 determinism; FR-8 explicitly excludes space-weather-driven models). It supplies the density consumed by the cannonball drag acceleration of Chapter 15 in the orbital regime, 1001000 km.
Formulation compatibility with Orekit's HarrisPriester class [11] is a de-
sign requirement: the frozen Phase 3 cross-tool drag case (exit criterion 5, decision D-15) uses Orekit as truth because GMAT does not implement Harris
Priester. The model is implemented in cpp/src/models/atmosphere_hp.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/atmosphere_hp.hpp.
13.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Mean solar activity. The committed coecient table is the Montenbruck
Gill mean-activity table; actual thermospheric density varies by factors of several with the solar cycle and geomagnetic activity. Montenbruck
and Gill place the model's representative accuracy near 1020 % for
91

the regimes it was tted to [38, Sect. 3.5.2]; treat absolute decay predictions accordingly.
2. Diurnal bulge only. The single harmonic cosn(/2) apex/antapex
modulation is the only local-time dependence; semiannual, 27-day, and geomagnetic variations are not modeled.
3. Static bulge geometry. The bulge apex is taken at the Sun's dec-
lination, lagging the Sun by 30 in right ascension (the thermospheric
response lag) [38, Sect. 3.5.2]; the same constant is used by the Orekit reference implementation [11].
4. Geodetic height argument. The table altitude is geodetic height
above the reference ellipsoid. This project evaluates it above the
WGS84 ellipsoid (a = 6 378 137.0 m, 1/f = 298.257223563 [42]; values in star/constants.hpp), matching the Orekit cross-tool congu-
ration. The density function itself takes the altitude as an argument, so a caller may supply a height computed against any ellipsoid.
5. Inclination-dependent exponent. The bulge exponent n ranges
from 2 for low-inclination orbits to 6 for polar orbits [38, Sect. 3.5.2].
The default is n = 4, adopted from the Orekit reference implementa-
tion [11] so that default congurations of the two tools coincide; mission conguration overrides it per orbit.
Domain of validity: geodetic altitude h  [100 km, 1000 km] (the table span) and n  [2, 6]. Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: below 100 km and for non-nite or out-of-range arguments (| cos | > 1, n < 2, n > 6) the model throws std::domain_error; above 1000 km it
returns exactly zero. Both choices mirror the Orekit reference implementation (which raises an altitude exception below the table and returns zero above it), keeping the cross-tool trajectories comparable; they are gated by
ATM-HP-DOMAIN.
13.3 Derivation
13.3.1 Antapex and apex proles

13.4 Discretization and implementation

1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/atmosphere_hp.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:hp:interp, eq:hp:cospow, eq:hp:density, eq:hp:apex, and eq:hp:geodetic verbatim.

2. Compiled-in table with a committed check copy. The 50-row
coecient table is compiled into the model source in kg m-3 (the book prints g km-3 = 10-12 kg m-3), digit-for-digit identical to the Orekit reference table. The committed golden tests/golden/atmosphere/harris_priester_table.toml is the independent transcription check: test ATM-HP-NODES requires the compiled table to match it bit-for-bit after strtod. A runtime le load
was rejected: the core never parses text (D-2).

Purity. 3.

The density function is a pure function of (geodetic alti-

tude, cos , n); the bulge-apex construction (equation (13.4)) and the

geodetic-altitude helper (equation (13.5)) are separate pure functions.

Frame handling and ellipsoid choice remain with the caller (the EOM

layer owns frames), which is what keeps the model testable against the

published values without an ephemeris in the loop.

4. Evaluation-order compatibility. Bracket search is a xed-order
forward scan; the interpolation is evaluated in the power form of equation (13.1); the bulge weight uses equation (13.2) with the reference
implementation's guard (weight set to zero when cos(/2)  10-12, i.e.
within double rounding of the exact antapex)  each choice mirrors Orekit [11] so cross-tool dierences reduce to oating-point rounding.

Determinism. 5.

Straight-line binary64 arithmetic, xed scan order, no

Chapter 14
Mars Atmosphere: Piecewise-Exponential Table
14.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the Mars atmosphere (FR-8, assumption A-3): a piecewise-exponential density table for aerobraking-class sensitivity studies in Mars orbit. Mars entry, descent, and landing is a project non-goal, so the model's only downstream consumer is the cannonball drag acceleration of Chapter 15 at orbital altitudes. The model is implemented in
cpp/src/models/atmosphere_mars.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/atmosphere_m
14.2 Assumptions and domain of validity Condence: low  provenance provisional per PRD A-3. This
entire model carries the PRD's assumption-A-3 ag, prominently and deliberately. The node densities derive from the NASA Glenn Research Center Mars Atmosphere Model curve ts [39]: an educational t to Mars Global Surveyor data (April 1996) that states no uncertainty, no altitude datum, no seasonal or diurnal qualication, and whose temperature t is discontin-
uous at its 7 km seam. It is a real, citable source and it is used honestly
 but it is not a validated engineering atmosphere model. The same ag is
carried in the golden manifest (tests/golden/atmosphere/manifest.toml)
and in the source header. Until a citable engineering provenance replaces it (A-3: reference TBD), results that depend on absolute Mars density are sensitivity studies, not predictions. Known context, for scale: the real Mars atmosphere varies seasonally by tens of percent in surface pressure and by
97

order-of-magnitude factors in upper-atmosphere density (dust storms); this static table represents none of that.
Assumptions:
1. Static, spherically uniform atmosphere  density is a function
of altitude alone.
2. Piecewise-exponential structure. Between committed nodes the
density is exponential in altitude; the per-segment scale height is derived from the adjacent node densities (equation (14.2)), which makes
the prole continuous at every boundary by construction.
3. Node truth equals the source curve t sampled at 5 km steps, 0 . 100 km The source temperature t crosses absolute zero near 112 km,
so the table is capped at 100 km, below the breakdown.
Domain of validity: altitude z  [0 km, 100 km] above the source model's
(unstated) surface reference. Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code
exactly: above 100 km the topmost segment's exponential is continued  a documented non-physical continuity aid whose scale height ( 41 km, an
artifact of the source t's collapsing temperature) is far larger than a physical Martian upper-atmosphere scale height; it exists so that aerobraking arcs with apoapsis above the table see a smooth, monotonically vanishing
density rather than a step. Below 0 km the rst segment's exponential is continued down to -8 km, comfortably below the deepest Martian terrain
(an engineering guard, not a physical datum); below that, and for non-nite
input, the model throws std::domain_error. Both behaviors are gated by ATM-MARS-DOMAIN.

14.3 Derivation
14.3.1 Source curve ts and node sampling
The NASA Glenn model [39], in metric form with altitude h in metres, is

14.4 Discretization and implementation
1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/atmosphere_mars.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:mars:glenn, eq:mars:scaleheight, and eq:mars:segment verbatim, and the le header carries the A-3
low-condence ag.
2. Bit-exact node table. The 21 node densities are compiled in as
C++17 hexadecimal oating literals, numerically identical to the com-
mitted golden (tests/golden/atmosphere/mars_nodes.toml, whose rho_kgpm3 hex elds are normative); test ATM-MARS-NODES enforces bit equality at every node. The segment coecients ki are computed
once from the nodes, in xed order, and cached (function-local static; single-threaded core, D-10).
3. Segment selection. Fixed-order forward scan for the segment with
zi  z; altitudes at or above the last node use the nal segment's
coecient (the documented extrapolation), and altitudes below node 0
use segment 0's coecient down to the -8 km guard.

99

4. Determinism. Straight-line binary64 arithmetic with libm log/exp
only; xed evaluation order; no data-dependent iteration counts.

Chapter 15
Cannonball Orbital Drag
15.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the cannonball atmospheric-drag acceleration (FR9): the orbital-regime drag model that consumes a density from one of the atmosphere models (Chapters 12, 13, and 14) and a ballistic parameter
CDA/m, mirroring the cannonball solar-radiation-pressure model's CRA/m.
FR-9 splits the aerodynamic domain deliberately: the Mach-table aerodynamic database (Phase 4) is valid for continuum ascent ight only, while this cannonball model serves the orbital free-molecular regime; the two never apply simultaneously, and a vehicle selects the cannonball model per cong-
uration. The model is implemented in cpp/src/models/drag.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/drag.hpp.
15.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Cannonball geometry. The drag force is attitude-independent: a
single constant product CDA/m characterizes the vehicle, as for a
sphere. For non-spherical vehicles this is the standard mean-area ap-
proximation; the error is absorbed into the congured CDA/m.
2. Co-rotating atmosphere (the FR-8 air-relative-velocity rule).
All aerodynamic quantities use the velocity of the vehicle relative to an atmosphere rotating rigidly with the planet, equation (15.3). Winds
are neglected; near-surface wind speeds (tens of m s-1) are two orders
101

below orbital air-relative speeds, and thermospheric super-rotation is far inside the density model's own uncertainty.
3. Free-molecular drag coecient. In the orbital regime the ow is
free-molecular (mean free path far exceeds vehicle dimensions; cf. the
USSA76 mean-free-path tables above 100 km [43]). The commonly adopted default for compact satellites is CD = 2.2, per the drag
discussions of Montenbruck and Gill [38, Sect. 3.5] and Vallado [57,
Sect. 8.6.2]; the value enters only through the congured CDA/m (the
default itself is applied at the vehicle-conguration level in Phase 4, not inside this function). Physical free-molecular values for non-compact shapes range roughly 2.03.0; treat absolute decay rates accordingly.
4. Frame-agnostic kinematics. The model is a pure function of (, CDA/m, vrel);
the EOM layer owns frames and supplies vrel resolved in the integration
frame, so the returned acceleration is in that same frame.
Domain of validity: orbital free-molecular ight around any body whose
atmosphere model supplies ; non-negative  and CDA/m. Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: negative  or negative CDA/m, and non-nite inputs, throw std::domain_error; a zero relative velocity returns
the exact zero vector (no normalization singularity exists because the for-
mulation never divides by vrel). Continuum ascent aerodynamics are ex-
plicitly outside this model's domain  they are the Phase 4 Mach-table database's regime (FR-9 domain split).

15.3 Derivation

Chapter 16
Composed Environment Force Model
16.1 Purpose This chapter documents the Phase 3 force-composition layer (cpp/src/models/environment.cpp):
the point-mass translational equations of motion about one central body (Earth, Moon, or Mars) under the FR-5..FR-9 environment models. No physics is derived here  every term's derivation, domain, and golden-vector evidence live in the per-model chapters (gravity, Chapter 9; third body, Chapter 10; SRP and shadow, Chapter 11; atmospheres, Chapters 12, 13, and 14; drag, Chapter 15). What is normative here, and nowhere else, is the
composition: the xed summation order, the frame and time plumbing each
term is evaluated through, the ephemeris body composition, the constants each term is wired to, and the documented approximations those choices introduce.
16.2 Assumptions and domain of validity 1. Point-mass spacecraft. The state is (r, v) in the GCRF-oriented
frame centered at the congured central body; attitude dynamics land in Phase 4. SRP and drag use the mass-normalized cannonball prod-
ucts CRA/m and CDA/m from the minimal [spacecraft] block.
2. One central body per run. SOI-event origin re-centering (FR-3) is
not part of Phase 3; a mission is Earth-, Moon-, or Mars-centered for its whole duration.
105

3. Inherited frame bounds. Earth-xed rotations use the IAU 2006/2000B
CIO chain with polar motion neglected and constant UT1 = 0 (bounds
in Chapter 5); the Moon principal-axis frame interpolates the DE440 libration angles; the Mars frame uses the IAU 2015 rotational elements [2].
4. Mars system barycenter. DE440 stores the Mars system barycen-
ter. Using it as the Mars body center osets the origin by the Pho-
bos/Deimos barycenter displacement, bounded by the mass ratios ( 2 Ṫ 10-4 m); the Mars system GM (GM4) is used consistently for both
the central point-mass tier and the Mars third body.
5. Documented composition approximations (each marked at its
site below): the multi-occulter illumination product, the USSA76 ceiling rule, and the Mars drag altitude datum.

16.3 Composition

The total acceleration is the xed-order sum (D-10: xed force-summation order, single-threaded)

(a) Central-body gravity. The pointmass tier applies a = -ṁ r/r3
(Chapter 2) with ṁ from the single constants home: the IERS value for j2 Earth [47] and the DE440 header values for Moon and Mars [45]. The and harmonic tiers rotate the position into the body-xed frame, evaluate
the Pines model of Chapter 9 on the loaded SRGRAV eld (whose own self-
consistent GM /R/coecient triple is used, per that chapter), and rotate the acceleration back: a = CT abf (C r) with C = CGbfCRF from Chapter 5.
(b) Third bodies. Each enabled perturber contributes the Battin f (q)

16.4 Discretization and implementation
Time ows from the mission epoch through the Phase 2 time systems (Chapter 3): the Python layer converts the UTC epoch to a two-part TAI epoch across the binding (the core never parses text, D-2); each right-hand-side
evaluation at mission-elapsed t forms TAI + t, from which the frame chain
takes TT and the ephemeris lookups take TDB seconds since J2000. The TDB epoch and the body-xed rotation are computed once per evaluation and shared by every term.
The model is evaluated through either integrator of Chapter 7 (FR-11): xed-step RK4 with truth records by step decimation (exactly the Phase 1 semantics), or adaptive RKF7(8) through the event-aware driver of Chapter 8 with truth records sampled from the cubic Hermite dense output at
k/ftruth. Dense-output interpolation error is bounded by h4/384 maxr(4) (Chapter 7), so hmax is the logging-accuracy control; the cross-tool missions pin hmax = 30 s (interpolation  2 Ṫ 10-2 m at LEO, far below the exit-
criterion gates). Construction loads the gravity eld and ephemeris before the time loop; evaluation performs no heap allocation and no le I/O (D-10).

Chapter 17
Rigid-Body Attitude Dynamics

17.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the rotational core of the FR-1 six-degree-of-freedom
vehicle model: the quaternion attitude kinematics and Euler's equation for
a rigid body with time-varying inertia, including the I term. The mod-
ule supplies the attitude piece of the vehicle equations of motion as a pure
right-hand-side map: given the attitude quaternion qŸi2b, the body rate B , the inertia tensor I , its time derivative I, and the total body torque  B , it returns (qŸ,  ) for embedding in a larger state vector. The Phase 4 vehicle layer supplies I , I, and  B from mass properties, actuators, and environmen-
tal torques (Chapter 18); this module depends on none of those structures.
It is implemented in cpp/src/models/rigidbody.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/rigidbody.hpp. The chapter also derives the
quaternion norm-drift bound that the FR-1 post-step normalization policy
rests on.

17.2 Assumptions and domain of validity

Assumptions:

1. Quasi-rigid body. The vehicle is rigid at every instant; mass varia-

tion enters only through the externally supplied pair I (t), I(t) , both

instantaneous expressed in body axes about the

center of mass, with

I symmetric positive denite and the pair mutually consistent (the

Phase 4 mass-properties model owns that consistency). Momentum

carried by internal relative motion of the depleting mass (propellant

111

swirl, jet damping) is excluded: the I form is the standard quasi-rigid
depletion approximation.
2. Torque completeness.  B is the total external plus actuator torque
about the instantaneous center of mass, resolved in body axes. The module does not distinguish torque sources.
3. Attitude convention. qŸi2b is the Hamilton, scalar-rst, inertial-to-
body frame-transformation quaternion of Section 1.4 (decision D-7);
B is the angular velocity of B with respect to I , resolved in B.
4. Norm handling. The kinematics of equation (17.2) is degree-one
homogeneous in qŸ and preserves qŸ exactly (equation (17.3)), so the
right-hand side is valid for any nonzero quaternion. Consumers of the attitude (the DCM of equation (1.7)) require unit norm; the post-step normalization policy of Section 17.4 maintains it.
Domain of validity: any state with I invertible. Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: a singular I makes the closed-form 3 Ṫ 3 inverse
divide by a zero determinant and IEEE non-nite values propagate; no righthand-side function of this module throws, because it runs inside the deterministic time loop and excluding non-physical mass properties is the conguration validator's job. The one between-step helper, post-step renormal-
ization, throws std::domain_error on a zero or non-nite quaternion norm rather than fabricating an attitude, mirroring star::rotation::quat_normalize:
a state that degenerate means the integration has already failed, and the deterministic response is a loud abort.

17.4 Discretization and implementation
There is no discretization: the module is a pointwise algebraic map, evaluated inside the vehicle right-hand side at whatever states the integrator (Chapter 7) requests. Implementation notes:
1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/rigidbody.cpp.
The source comments echo the labels eq:rigidbody:qdot, eq:rigidbody:euler, eq:rigidbody:omegadot, and eq:rigidbody:normdrift verbatim.
2. Packed state slice. The raw-pointer entry point rigidbody_rhs
operates on the seven-component slice [qw, qx, qy, qz , x, y, z ] (scalar-
rst, per Table 1.2 rule 1), the layout the Phase 4 vehicle state vector embeds.
3. Explicit 3 Ṫ 3 inverse. The solve in equation (17.5) uses the closed-
form cofactor inverse (Eigen::Matrix3d::inverse()): IEEE basic op-
erations only, in a xed order, no pivot search, no allocation  the
relative error is bounded by a small multiple of (I ) , and physical inertia tensors are well conditioned ( < 102 for any credible vehicle).

116

4. No normalization inside the right-hand side. Normalizing qŸ

inside the RHS would change the ODE the integrator sees and cor-

rupt the embedded error estimate; by equation (17.3) it is also un-

between necessary. Normalization is applied

steps by the propaga-

tion layer via rigidbody_renormalize, which returns the signed pre-

normalization deviation qŸ - 1 so callers can monitor the documented

drift bound (17.16).

Determinism. 5.

No heap allocation, single-threaded, xed evaluation

order, IEEE basic operations only (D-10); the golden generator's mp-

math mirror reproduces the same formulation from the same commit-

ted binary64 inputs.

Chapter 18
Gravity-Gradient Torque
18.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the gravity-gradient torque model (FR-1): the torque a nite rigid body experiences about its center of mass because the central body's gravitational eld is stronger on the near side than on the far side. It is the one environmental torque the PRD models  on-orbit aerodynamic, solar-radiation-pressure, and magnetic disturbance torques are Non-Goals (their exclusion is bounded in Section 18.2). The model is implemented in
cpp/src/models/gravgrad.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/gravgrad.hpp; it is purely algebraic in its inputs (ṁ, rI , qŸi2b, I )  the gravitational param-
eter of the current central body, the central-body-to-vehicle position in the inertial frame, the attitude, and the inertia tensor, all quantities the FR-1 state and mass-property layers already carry  and depends on no environment or vehicle structure. The chapter also derives the pitch-libration frequency of a gravity-gradient stabilized body, the analytic reference for Phase 4 exit criterion 9.
18.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Point-mass central eld. The torque is computed from the spher-
ically symmetric -ṁr/r3 eld. The eld's harmonic structure (Chap-
ter 9) also has a gradient across the body, but its contribution is smaller than the retained term by the relative size of the harmonic eld itself,
O J2(R/r)2  10-3 in LEO, and is neglected  consistent with the
standard formulation.
119

2. First-order tidal expansion. The eld is linearized across the body:
for a vehicle of extent c at distance r, the rst neglected term is smaller by O(c/r) ( 10-6 for c  10 m in LEO). The expansion is the same
tidal limit as the third-body discussion of Chapter 10, applied here to the attitude channel.
3. Torque about the instantaneous center of mass, with I the same
center-of-mass, body-axes inertia tensor the dynamics of Chapter 17
uses, and r the vector from the current central body to the vehicle (FR-
1: "about the current central body, using states and inertia already
available"). Only the direction of r and its magnitude enter.
4. Unit attitude quaternion. qŸi2b carries the caller's unit-norm in-
variant (maintained by the FR-1 post-step normalization); a non-unit
quaternion scales the returned torque by qŸ4 (the DCM enters twice), a relative error of 4(qŸ - 1) for small deviations  negligible under
the drift bound of Chapter 17 but stated so the invariant is explicit.
5. Prescribed-orbit libration analysis. The libration derivation of prescribed Section 18.3.2 and its validation test place the body on a
circular orbit of radius r with mean motion n = ṁ/r3: attitude
does not feed back into translation. This is the module-level validation conguration; the fully coupled translationalrotational vehicle lands with the Phase 4 integration workstream, and the attitude-to-orbit
coupling neglected here is of relative order (c/r)2 in the orbit.

Excluded-torque bounds, recorded once so the exclusion is quantitative:

for a vehicle of characteristic area A, center-of-pressure oset d, and residual

dipole m, the excluded torques are bounded by srp  P1auAd (1 + CR) with

P1au

=

the vehicle's residual dipole and the local eld (no eld model ships with the
core). For a representative 100 kg-class LEO vehicle (A  1 m2, d  0.1 m, I  100 kg m2) the modeled gravity-gradient torque at r = 7 Ṫ 106 m is of order 3ṁ I /(2r3)  7 Ṫ 10-5 N m, one to two orders above the SRP bound ( 1Ṫ10-6 N m) and above the aero bound outside the densest drag regimes.

Domain of validity: any state with r = 0. Out-of-domain behavior,

matching the code exactly: at r = 0 the normalization divides by zero and

IEEE non-nite values propagate; the model does not throw (deterministic-

loop rule; a spacecraft coincident with a body center is excluded by cong-

uration validation, as in Chapter 10).

18.4 Discretization and implementation
There is no discretization: the model is a pointwise algebraic map from
(ṁ, rI , qŸi2b, I ) to  B . Implementation notes:
122

1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/gravgrad.cpp;
the source comments echo eq:gravgrad:torque verbatim, and the validation test echoes eq:gravgrad:pitch, eq:gravgrad:libfreq, and eq:gravgrad:pendulum.
2. Evaluation order. The position is normalized in the inertial frame
(r^I = r/r) and rotated with star::rotation::quat_transform, the
single project code path for frame transformation (Chapter 4), then contracted per equation (18.5). Fixed order, IEEE basic operations plus one square root, no allocation (D-10).
3. Scale factor once. 3ṁ/r3 is formed as one scalar and applied to the
cross product, so the structural zeros of the property tests (spherical
I , principal-axis alignment) are exact: every oating-point product in
the cross-product dierence either carries a zero factor or subtracts two identically rounded copies of the same real product.
4. Data ownership. ṁ is supplied by the caller (the force-composition
layer passes the current central body's value); the module denes no body constants.

the properties of equation (18.5). Phase 4 exit criterion 9: the libration frequency of a gravity-gradient-stabilized body on the prescribed circular reference orbit, measured from
event-located pitch zero crossings over 11 periods, matches the analytic lib of equation (18.7) to
within 0.1 % (the known nite-amplitude oset is
2.5 Ṫ 10-5), and matches the amplitude-corrected pend of equation (18.8) to within 10-7 relative.

Chapter 19
Vehicle Mass Properties
19.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the analytic settled-tank mass-properties model (FR-10): the closed forms that supply the composite vehicle mass, center of gravity, inertia tensor, and their exact time derivatives to the rigid-body
dynamics (Euler's equation with the I term, FR-1) and to the staging
state remap (FR-10). A vehicle is a collection of rigid bodies resolved in
the single structural frame of FR-13 (+X forward): per-stage dry bodies,
attached jettisonable items, and one settled-propellant slug per cylindrical tank. Depletion moves the composite CG continuously; jettison changes the composite discretely in closed form. The model is implemented in
cpp/src/models/massprops.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/massprops.hpp.
19.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Settled propellant (assumption A-2). The liquid in each tank is
a rigid slug resting against the aft (-X ) tank face, as under sustained
axial thrust acceleration. Slosh, ullage gas, and pressurant mass are not modeled; their omission is acceptable for the v1 ascent and orbit studies A-2 scopes this model to.
2. Cylindrical tanks with axis along +X. Each tank is a right cir-
cular cylinder whose axis is parallel to the vehicle +X axis. This is
a deliberate v1 restriction: the closed forms below are specic to that
125

po- geometry, and the tank parameter struct documents it. O-X tank sitions (transverse osets of the axis) are fully supported; o-X tank orientations are not.
3. Rigid bodies, constant dry properties. Dry-body masses, CGs,
and inertia tensors (about each body's own CG, resolved in the vehicle frame) are constants supplied by the conguration; only the propellant slugs vary in time.
4. Homogeneous propellant. Each slug has the constant bulk density
of its tank's propellant; thermal density variation is absorbed into the congured density.
Domain of validity: propellant mass mp  [0, R2L] per tank (ll height
inside the cylinder); positive tank radius, length, and density; non-negative body masses with at least one strictly positive mass in any composition; removal mass strictly below the composite mass. Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: non-nite inputs, non-positive tank dimensions or density, negative masses, propellant beyond capacity, an empty body list, a non-positive composite mass, and a removal that would leave a non-positive
remainder all throw std::domain_error. An exactly empty tank (mp = 0)
is in-domain and yields a zero-mass slug whose CG sits at the aft-face center and whose inertia and rates are exactly zero.

19.4 Discretization and implementation
1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/massprops.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:massprops:fillheight through eq:massprops:remove verbatim.
2. Exact wet-mass identity. The slug mass is the propellant-mass ar-
gument passed through verbatim  it is never reconstructed as R2h
from the ll height, which would add two roundings  and the composite mass is the plain sum of the body masses in the caller's vector
exactly order. The wet mass at t0 therefore equals dry plus propellant
(bit-level) for any same-order binary64 sum, the Phase 4 exit-criterion2 identity.

128

3. Fixed summation order (D-10). All compositions iterate the body
vector in index order; callers list xed bodies rst and tank slugs after, and the convention is documented at the API so two call sites cannot disagree.
4. No nite dierencing. I and cŸ are the closed forms (19.3) and
(19.6); the validation suite cross-checks them against central dierences of the composite properties as an independent (dierent-mathematics) reference.
5. Determinism. Fixed-order sums and products with no libm calls;
every operation is an IEEE-754 basic operation, so the module is bitportable across platforms under the D-10 ags.

Chapter 20
Engine Propulsion and Thrust-Vector Control
20.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the FR-10 engine model: per-engine delivered thrust with ambient back-pressure, mass ow from the constant vacuum specic impulse, throttle limits, linear spool-up and spool-down ramps, ignition-count enforcement, and gimbal (TVC) angle and rate limits. The engine produces a body force and a torque about the current composite CG (Chapter 19) and a propellant mass-ow rate that drives the settled-tank depletion. The
model is implemented in cpp/src/models/propulsion.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/propulsion.hpp.
20.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Constant vacuum specic impulse. Each engine's Isp,vac is con-
stant over its throttle range (FR-10): chamber conditions scale proportionally with throttle, so vacuum thrust and mass ow scale together.
Real engines lose a few seconds of Isp at deep throttle; that error is
absorbed into the congured rating.
2. Back pressure acts only on delivered thrust. The ambient term
pambAe is the static-pressure force on the nozzle exit plane; it does
not alter the internal ow, so the mass ow follows the vacuum rating
131

and throttle only (equation (20.2)). Flow separation in heavily overexpanded operation is not modeled; the delivered thrust may go negative if an engine is run at low throttle deep in an atmosphere, and the conguration layer is responsible for physically sensible throttle oors.
3. Rigid TVC geometry. The engine is mounted at a xed position
with a xed nominal thrust axis in the vehicle frame (FR-13, +X
forward); gimbal deection rotates the thrust direction but not the application point. Inertial (tail-wags-dog) eects of the swiveling engine mass are not modeled.
4. Quasi-static throttle response. Spool-up and spool-down are linear
ramps of the delivered throttle level between 0 and the commanded setting (FR-10); combustion transients are not modeled.
Domain of validity: non-negative vacuum thrust and exit area; positive
Isp,vac; throttle limits 0  min  max  1; unit-norm nominal axis and mu-
tually orthogonal unit gimbal axes; non-negative spool times, gimbal limit,
and gimbal rate; ambient pressure pamb  0 supplied by the atmosphere
model in use (USSA76 for Earth ascent, Chapter 12). Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: non-nite inputs, negative ratings, malformed axis vectors, inverted throttle limits, and negative step sizes throw
std::domain_error. A zero delivered throttle level returns exactly zero
force, torque, and mass ow  an engine that is o exerts no back-pressure force because its nozzle is not owing.

20.3 Derivation

20.3.1 Delivered thrust and mass ow

Consider a steady control volume enclosing the engine, cut at the nozzle exit
plane of area Ae. Momentum conservation for exhaust leaving at eective exhaust speed ve with mass ow m and exit static pressure pe, immersed in ambient pressure pamb (which acts on every outer surface of the vehicle and
leaves only the exit-plane imbalance uncancelled), gives the delivered thrust

F = m ve + (pe - pamb) Ae.
Dene the vacuum thrust at the same operating point, Fvac = m ve+peAe, i.e.
the thrust the same chamber state delivers with pamb = 0. With a throttle level  scaling the chamber mass ow (and hence Fvac) proportionally,

F =  Fvac - pamb Ae ( > 0); F = 0 ( = 0).

(20.1)

132

The vacuum specic impulse is dened by Fvac = m g0 Isp,vac with the standard gravity g0 = 9.806 65 m s-2 exact (the conventional value xed by the

3rd CGPM, 1901, as published in the SI Brochure [8]). Solving for the mass

ow at throttle :

m =  Fvac . g0 Isp,vac

(20.2)

delivered back pressure reduces the

consumption (20.2). Equivalently, the delivered specic impulse F /(m g0)

falls with altitude while Isp,vac stays constant.

20.3.2 Gimbal deection and force/torque coupling

The engine's nominal thrust direction is the unit vector u^ (vehicle frame; +X for an aft-mounted main engine). TVC deects it by two gimbal angles (1, 2) about two congured orthogonal unit axes a^1, a^2 perpendicular to u^ (defaults +Y , +Z ), applied in that xed order with the Rodrigues rotation R(a^, )v = v cos  + (a^ Ṫ v) sin  + a^(a^ Ṗ v)(1 - cos ):

d^ = R(a^2, 2) R(a^1, 1) u^.

(20.3)

20.4 Discretization and implementation

1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/propulsion.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:propulsion:thrust through eq:propulsion:gimbalslew verbatim.

2. State advance vs. pure evaluation. The actuator state (running
ag, ignition count, delivered throttle level, gimbal angles) advances once per step by a discrete update; force, torque, and mass ow are pure functions of parameters and state so the integrator may evaluate them at any stage without side eects (D-2 core discipline: plain structs in, plain structs out).

Spool ramp. 3.

The delivered level  slews linearly toward the target

 = clamp(cmd, min, max) while running and toward 0 when shut

down, at the congured full-range rates:

 =  + clamp  - , -t/tdown, +t/tup ,

(20.6)

where tup (tdown) is the 0-to-1 (1-to-0) spool time; a zero spool time
applies the target immediately. The ramp is exactly linear: away from
the endpoints each step adds exactly t/tup.
4. Ignition count. A run command on a non-running engine consumes
one ignition; when the congured count is exhausted the command is
refused and the engine stays o (the level target remains 0). Shutting
down mid-spool and re-igniting consumes a new count.
5. Gimbal slew and clamp. Each gimbal angle slews toward its com-
mand at exactly the congured rate and is clamped at the angle limit, per axis:

i = clamp i+clamp(cmd,i-i, - maxt, + maxt), -max, +max .
(20.7) A step command therefore produces a ramp whose per-step increment
is exactly  maxt until the nal partial step (Phase 4 exit criterion 7).
The angle limit is a per-axis (square) clamp, not a cone.
6. Determinism. The only libm calls are the sin / cos pair per gimbal
axis in (20.3); everything else is IEEE-754 basic operations in xed order. Zero throttle returns literal zeros.

Chapter 21
RCS Thrusters and Reaction Wheels

21.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the FR-1 attitude actuators: on/o reaction control thrusters grouped in clusters, with minimum-impulse-bit (MIB) enforcement and full force-and-torque coupling about the current composite CG, and reaction wheels with per-wheel momentum states and exact torque and momentum saturation, including the total-system angular-momentum bookkeeping that makes conservation testable. Both actuators are implemented in
cpp/src/models/actuators.cpp with the interface in cpp/include/star/models/actuators.hpp.

21.2 Assumptions and domain of validity

Assumptions:

1. Ideal rectangular RCS pulses. A ring thruster delivers its rated
constant thrust along a xed unit direction at a xed position in the ve-
hicle frame (FR-13, +X forward); valve opening and closing transients
are collapsed into the MIB rule. Thruster propellant consumption is not modeled in v1 (RCS propellant budgets are orders below mainengine ow for the FR-13 vehicle class); the delivered momentum is nevertheless exact, so conservation checks remain meaningful.

2. Minimum impulse bit as a hard oor. A commanded pulse whose

ideal impulse (thrust times duration) falls below the congured MIB

exactly zero delivers

impulse  the valve never eectively opens 

137

and a pulse at or above the MIB delivers exactly thrust times duration. Real thrusters deliver a degraded, poorly repeatable impulse near the MIB; the model replaces that gray zone with a deterministic threshold, documented so control designers treat the MIB as unusable resolution.
3. Rigid momentum-exchange wheels. Each wheel spins about a
xed unit axis in the vehicle frame and stores the relative angular mo-
mentum hw along that axis; the wheel's contribution to the composite
inertia is part of the congured dry-body inertia. Motor torque is internal to the vehicle: the reaction on the body is exactly the negative of the torque on the wheel, following the standard momentum-exchange formulation of Markley and Crassidis [35]. Wheel friction and drag torques are not modeled.
4. Saturation semantics (documented choice). Delivered wheel torque
is clamped at the congured torque limit, and the stored momentum is limited at the congured momentum rail: a step that would cross the rail delivers only the torque that lands the momentum exactly on the rail, and a wheel starting on the rail delivers exactly zero torque for a same-sign command (it cannot accept further momentum of that sign) while opposite-sign (desaturating) commands act normally.
Domain of validity: unit-norm thruster directions and wheel axes; nonnegative thrust, MIB, pulse duration, torque limit, and momentum limit; strictly positive step size for the wheel update; initial wheel momentum
within [-hmax, +hmax]. Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code ex-
actly: non-nite inputs, malformed unit vectors, negative ratings or durations, non-positive step sizes, and an initial momentum outside the rails
throw std::domain_error.

21.3 Derivation

21.3.1 RCS pulse impulse and coupling

A thruster with rated thrust F and unit direction d^ red for a duration T

ideally delivers the impulse magnitude F T . With the congured minimum

impulse bit Jmin:

0, J=

F T < Jmin,

F T, F T  Jmin.

(21.1)

the pulse (the geometry is constant during the pulse at the FR-1 modeling

level) gives the linear and angular impulse delivered to the body,

p = J d^, L = (rt - cŸ) Ṫ p,

(21.2)

where rt is the thruster position. Because thrusters are generally not mounted
through the CG, every pulse couples force and torque; a cluster sums (21.2)
over its active thrusters in conguration order. While a thruster is held on
continuously the body sees the constant force F d^ and torque (rt - cŸ) Ṫ F d^,
the integrands of (21.2).

21.3.3 Total angular momentum bookkeeping

With body inertia I (about the composite CG), body angular velocity , and n wheels, the total angular momentum of the vehicle-plus-wheels system,
resolved in the body frame, is

n

i=1

(21.5)

the standard momentum-exchange decomposition [35] (the wheels' trans-
verse and structural inertia are inside I ; the hw,i are the wheels' spin mo-
menta relative to the body). Under zero external torque the inertially re-

because H +  Ṫ H = 0: the wheel terms ḟ a^ cancel between I  and h wa^.
This identity is the Phase 4 exit-criterion-7 conservation gate and the reason the bookkeeping function ships with the model rather than with the tests.

21.4 Discretization and implementation

1. Module and traceability. Both actuators live in cpp/src/models/actuators.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:actuators:mib through eq:actuators:totalmomentum
verbatim.

2. Exact thresholds and rails. The MIB branch (21.1) returns literal
zeros below the threshold, and the rail branches of (21.3) assign the congured limit itself (not an accumulated sum), so refusal, saturation, and rail states are bit-exact and reproducible (D-10).

3. Pure functions over plain structs. Thruster and wheel parame-
ters are trivially constructible structs mirroring the FR-13 vocabulary;
the wheel update is (params, command, state, t)  (delivered, state)
with no globals or I/O (D-2). Cluster sums iterate thrusters in cong-
uration order.

Determinism. 4.

No libm calls anywhere in the module; every operation

is an IEEE-754 basic operation in xed order, so the module is bit-

portable across platforms under the D-10 ags.

including o-CG and retrograde directions and a cluster sum. Torque and momentum clamp exactly at the congured saturations per (21.3): over-limit commands
deliver exactly ḟmax, rail landings set the momentum exactly to ḟhmax, a same-sign command on
the rail delivers exactly zero, and desaturating commands act normally (Phase 4 exit criterion 7), all against committed golden vectors. A three-axis rigid-body slew driven through the wheel model (RK4, quaternion attitude, gyroscopic coupling active) conserves the inertially resolved to-
tal momentum (21.5) to 10-12 relative over the full
maneuver, and the reaction sign (21.4) moves body and wheel momentum in opposite directions (Phase 4 exit criterion 7). Out-of-domain inputs per Section 21.2 throw
std::domain_error.

141

Chapter 22
Axisymmetric Ascent Aerodynamics
22.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the FR-9 continuum ascent aerodynamics model: the body-frame aerodynamic force and the moment about the current composite center of gravity (CG) of an axisymmetric launch vehicle, evalu-
ated from a per-stack-conguration Mach-table database CA(M ), CN (M ), xcp(M ) with an optional constant pitch-damping derivative Cmq , using the
total-angle-of-attack formulation. The database is congured by the FR-13
vehicle schema's [[aero]] blocks and their CSV Mach tables; this model is
the ascent-regime counterpart of the cannonball orbital-drag model (Chapter 15), and the two regimes never apply simultaneously (the FR-9 domain
split). The model is implemented in cpp/src/models/aero.cpp with its interface in cpp/include/star/models/aero.hpp.
22.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Axisymmetric conguration, total-angle-of-attack loading. The
stack is aerodynamically axisymmetric about the structural +X axis (FR-13: +X toward the nose, origin at the aft plane). The loading
then depends on Mach number and on the single total angle of attack
t between +x^ and the air-relative velocity; by symmetry the resultant force lies in the wind plane spanned by x^ and vrel. There is no
142

side force out of that plane and no aerodynamic roll torque (no ns,
no Clp): the torque x-component is structurally zero.
2. Air-relative velocity supplied by the caller (the FR-8 rule).
All aerodynamic quantities  Mach number, dynamic pressure, angle of attack  use the air-relative velocity of a co-rotating atmo-
sphere, vrel = v -p Ṫr (Chapter 15, equation eq:drag:vrel), which the
equations-of-motion layer computes and rotates into the body frame;
this module is frame-agnostic given the body-frame vrel. Winds are neglected, as in Chapter 15. The density  and speed of sound a come
from the atmosphere models (Chapter 12 provides both for Earth ascent).
3. Normal force linear in sin t (documented choice). The database
carries the normal-force slope CN (M ) per radian and the model evaluates CN = CN (M ) sin t. This is the standard slender-body crossow form: it is odd in t, matches the linear-in- slope at small angles to within t3/6 (relative error  0.5 % at t = 10), is algebraically free
of normalization singularities (Section 22.3), and degrades gracefully
toward the crossow-only geometry at t  90. The database itself
is tted for the small-to-moderate angles of ascent ight; evaluations
at large t are a geometric extension of the formulation, not data.
4. Composite CG on the symmetry axis. The moment uses only
the axial CG station xcg : the axial force acts along the symmetry
axis and therefore produces no moment about an on-axis CG, and
the normal force acts at the center-of-pressure station xcp(M ) on the
axis. Lateral CG osets of the FR-13 stacks (whose sub-blocks are nominally axisymmetric) are neglected; the induced moment error is
of order (lateral oset) Ṫ (force), second-order for near-axis CGs.
5. Quasi-steady coecients with optional constant pitch damping. Unsteady eects are collapsed into the single optional constant
Cmq (per radian of nondimensional pitch rate q^ =  dref /(2vrel), referenced to Sref and the reference diameter dref  the convention declared for the vehicle schema's cmq_per_rad key). Cmq  0 opposes
the transverse rate; exactly zero disables the term. The roll rate is undamped (assumption 1).
6. Piecewise-linear Mach interpolation, clamped ends (documented approximation). Coecients between breakpoints are piecewise-
linear in Mach; below the rst and above the last breakpoint the end
143

row is held constant. Both choices are deterministic, continuous, and exact at the breakpoints (Section 22.4).
Domain of validity: continuum ascent ight only  the orbital freemolecular regime is Chapter 15's cannonball model (FR-9 domain split)  in forward ight at the small-to-moderate total angles of attack for which a linear normal-force-slope database is meaningful, with Mach inside the congured table (clamped outside, per assumption 6). Zero air-relative velocity (the vehicle on the pad before release) returns exactly zero force, moment, Mach, dynamic pressure, and angle of attack. Out-of-domain behavior, matching the code exactly: malformed tables (fewer than two rows, columnlength mismatches, a non-increasing or negative Mach grid, non-nite en-
tries, non-positive Sref or dref , positive Cmq ) and malformed inputs (nonnite velocity, rates, or CG station; negative or non-nite ; non-positive or non-nite a; a negative or non-nite Mach passed to the coecient lookup) throw std::domain_error.

22.3.1 Air data and total angle of attack

22.3.2 Force decomposition

For an axisymmetric body the pressure and shear distribution is invariant
under a rotation about x^ applied jointly to the body and the wind vector,
so the resultant force lies in the wind plane and is fully described by two dimensionless coecients on the dynamic pressure and the congured refer-
ence area Sref [38, Sect. 3.5], [57, Sect. 8.6.2]: an axial force coecient CA

144

along -x^ and a normal force coecient CN in the wind plane, perpendic-
ular to the axis, opposing the crossow. With the database convention of
assumption 3, CN = CN(M ) sin t:

FA = - qŸSref CA(M ) x^,

where the second form of (22.5) substitutes sin t from (22.3) and absorbs
the crossow normalization: it involves no trigonometric evaluation and no
division by v, so zero crossow yields an exactly zero normal force with
no special case, and the only excluded point of the whole formulation is
v = 0, which returns the structural zero of Section 22.2. The total force is F = FA + FN .

22.3.3 Center-of-pressure moment
The database locates the resultant normal force at the center-of-pressure
station xcp(M ) on the symmetry axis, expressed in the same structural frame as every vehicle station (origin at the aft plane, +X toward the nose  exactly the xcp_m column the vehicle schema declares). With the composite CG at station xcg on the axis (assumption 4), the moment about the CG is
the lever arm crossed with the normal force:

mcp = xcp(M ) - xcg x^ Ṫ FN .

(22.6)

The axial force contributes no moment (it acts along the axis through the
on-axis CG), so t = 0 produces exactly zero static moment. When the center of pressure is forward of the CG (xcp > xcg ), (22.6) is an overturning
(destabilizing) moment  the normal case for the nless launchers of the
starter eet, which are stabilized by thrust-vector control; xcp < xcg gives a
restoring moment.

22.3.4 Pitch-damping moment
The optional damping term models the moment that opposes the transverse
angular rate. Using the classical rate nondimensionalization q^ =  dref /(2v) with the congured reference diameter dref , the damping contribution to the moment coecient about each transverse axis is Cmq q^, i.e. a dimensional moment qŸSref dref Ṗ Cmq dref /(2v) per transverse axis. Applied isotropically

part of the body angular velocity:

22.3.5 Mach-table interpolation

Each coecient column c  {CA, CN , xcp} is tabulated on one strictly increasing Mach grid M1 < M2 < Ṗ Ṗ Ṗ < Mn (n  2, M1  0). The lookup is
piecewise linear with clamped ends:

c1,   
c(M ) = ci + u (ci+1 - ci),
   cn,

u = M - Mi , Mi+1 - Mi

M  M1, Mi  M < Mi+1, M  Mn.

(22.8)

The interpolant is continuous everywhere, including at the clamp junctions,

and exact at every breakpoint: the clamp branches return the end rows
literally, and an interior breakpoint selects its own segment with u = 0, so ci + u(ci+1 - ci) reproduces ci exactly in IEEE arithmetic.

22.4 Discretization and implementation
1. Module and traceability. The model lives in cpp/src/models/aero.cpp;
the source comments echo the labels eq:aero:mach through eq:aero:damping
verbatim.
2. Structural zeros. v = 0 returns literal zeros in every output before
any table access  the logged dynamic pressure on the pad is exactly
zero (Phase 4 exit criterion 10). Zero crossow (vy = vz = 0) skips the
normal-force/center-of-pressure block entirely, leaving literal zeros (ax-
ial force only); Cmq = 0 or a purely axial rate skips the damping block; the torque x-component is never written (no roll torque, assumption
1). These are branch decisions on exact binary64 comparisons, not epsilon tests.

146

3. Fixed evaluation order. Segment selection scans the grid in as-
cending order; every product chain is written in one xed association. Together with the exact-breakpoint property of (22.8), evaluation at a committed table breakpoint reads the table row exactly.
4. Determinism. The force/moment path uses IEEE-754 basic oper-
ations and square roots only (Eigen's norm()), so it is bit-portable across platforms under the D-10 ags. The reported t diagnostic (22.3) is the module's only libm call (atan2); it is never consumed
by the force/moment path, so its one-ulp cross-platform spread never feeds back into the dynamics.
5. Pure function over plain structs. The table struct mirrors the FR-
13 vocabulary (ref_area_m2, ref_diameter_m, cmq_per_rad, and the CSV columns mach, ca, cnalpha_per_rad, xcp_m); the Python layer
validates and lls it across the binding (D-2: the core never parses
text). The caller supplies the body-frame vrel (FR-8),  and a from the atmosphere model, the CG station xcg from the mass-property model (Chapter 19), and the body rates; selecting the active [[aero]]
conguration across staging events is the vehicle layer's responsibility.

Table 22.1 lists the tests that constitute this chapter's validation evidence.
Each test identier is machine-checked to exist in the test tree by scripts/lint_chapters.py; golden provenance and tolerances are recorded in tests/golden/aero/manifest.toml.
22.6 References
The dynamic-pressure dimensionless-coecient force convention follows Montenbruck and Gill [38, Sect. 3.5] and Vallado [57, Sect. 8.6.2], the same convention already relied on by Chapter 15. The axisymmetric total-angle-ofattack decomposition (22.4)(22.5) is derived in Section 22.3 from the symmetry of the congured vehicle; the center-of-pressure moment (22.6) and the pitch-damping nondimensionalization (22.7) are the coecient-database conventions this project declares for the FR-13 vehicle schema (documented choices of this chapter, not external physical results). The committed eet tables carry provenance representative in their CSV headers. Full bibliographic details appear in the bibliography.

Chapter 23
Vehicle 6DOF Composition
23.1 Purpose
This chapter documents the composition layer that assembles the individual force, torque, and mass-property models into a full launch-to-orbit-capable six-degree-of-freedom vehicle run (FR-1, FR-8FR-10, FR-12, FR-14). Every physical term is derived in its own chapter  the composed environment (Chapter 16), gravity-gradient torque (Chapter 18), rigid-body attitude dynamics (Chapter 17), settled-tank mass properties (Chapter 19), engine propulsion (Chapter 20), attitude actuators (Chapter 21), and axisymmetric aerodynamics (Chapter 22). This chapter owns only the geometry and bookkeeping the run path adds on top of them: the geodetic launch-pad initial state, the open-loop pitch-program attitude command, the xed-order translational acceleration assembly, and the closed-form staging/jettison state remap. The load-bearing pure pieces are implemented in
cpp/src/models/vehicle6dof.cpp; the stepping, control-cycle zero-order hold, event sequence, and logging orchestration live in cpp/src/run.cpp (run_vehicle).
23.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Continuous state and control cycle. The integrated continu-
ous state is the translational pair y = [rI , vI ] (equation (23.1)), the
central-body-centered GCRF position and velocity of the composite center of mass, advanced with the xed-step RK4 of Chapter 7. At-
titude (qŸi2b, B ), the per-tank propellant masses, and the per-engine
149

spool/gimbal/ignition states are advanced once per control cycle and held constant across the cycle (D-5 zero-order hold); the composite mass properties are likewise held over the cycle. For the reference missions the cycle equals the RK4 step, so the intra-step variation of the gravity, thrust back-pressure, and aerodynamic terms is resolved while the commanded attitude, throttle, and mass are piecewise constant.
2. Prescribed open-loop attitude. With no GNC component in the
loop (Phase 4), the attitude is prescribed each cycle by the active sequence command  pad-xed, pitch-program, inertial-hold, or ratecommand  rather than integrated from the rotational equation of motion. The rigid-body attitude dynamics of Chapter 17, including the gravity-gradient torque of Chapter 18, are validated as free dynamics at module level (exit criterion 9); the closed-loop attitude-control path lands with the Phase 6 GNC workstream.
3. Fixed force-summation order (D-10). The translational accelera-
tion sums the environment acceleration (itself in the xed internal order of Chapter 16) and then the body force in the order thrust, RCS, aero; the rotational torque, when integrated, sums gravity-gradient, engine gimbal, RCS, wheel reaction, and aero moment in that order. The order is xed so a run is bit-reproducible.
4. Air-relative velocity for air data. Mach number and dynamic
pressure use the co-rotating air-relative velocity vrel = v - planet Ṫ r
(FR-8, equation (15.3)), resolved into body axes and passed to the aerodynamics model of Chapter 22; the logged Mach and dynamic pressure are that model's own outputs. The logged ight-path angle uses the
inertial velocity,  = arcsin (r Ṗ v)/(r v) , the standard trajectory di-
agnostic; the two conventions are stated here and applied consistently
by run_vehicle.
5. Inertially xed launch tangent frame. The pitch-program east/north/up
basis is evaluated at the launch site at t0 and held inertially xed for the ascent; the Earth rotates  1.25 over a ve-minute ascent, a bounded
approximation of the pad-tangent frame recorded here.
6. Settled propellant, mass drop on separation. Tank mass prop-
erties are the settled-cylinder forms of Chapter 19 (A-2); a separated stage is removed from the simulation (mass drop only, A-4), and its discarded dynamics are not propagated.
150

Domain of validity: the geodetic launch form requires an Earth central body and a well-conditioned attitude (the pad up-direction is nonzero by construction). The composed-acceleration and remap forms require a positive composite mass, which the mass-property composition guarantees while any body remains attached; a conguration that removes the last body is rejected
by Chapter 19. The SOI-transition geometry is dened for the EarthMoon
case used by the trans-lunar mission and requires the committed ephemeris excerpt.

tude, throttle, gimbal, and mass are the zero-order-hold values of the cycle.

d^I = cos  sin A e^I + cos A n^ I + sin  u^I ,

so  = 90 is vertical (thrust along local up) at lifto. The attitude qŸi2b is then constructed with body +X along d^I , completing the triad by Gram Schmidt of a reference direction against d^I (equation (23.5)); since the aero-
dynamics and thrust are axisymmetric about body +X , the roll orientation
is a free, deterministic choice (Markley and Crassidis [35]). Writing the body

Equation (23.5) is undened at  = 90. There x^ = u^I , the numera-
tor vanishes identically, and a generic construction must fall back to some
reference unrelated to the ight azimuth  so the roll re-resolves, discon-
tinuously, on the rst cycle that leaves the vertical. The pitch program
does not need that fallback, because its azimuth is commanded rather than
inferred. Substituting x^ from equation (23.4) into equation (23.5), and writing h^ I = sin A e^I + cos A n^ I for the ground-track direction, the numerator is

cos  (cos  u^I - sin  h^ I ), whose norm is |cos |, so for cos  > 0 the Gram

y^ = cos  u^I - sin  h^ I ,

(23.6)

which is unit and orthogonal to x^ for every , and at  = 90 reduces to -h^ I :
the commanded azimuth still xes the roll, and the commanded attitude is
continuous through a true vertical hold. The implementation evaluates equa-
tion (23.5) directly where it is well conditioned and equation (23.6) where it
is not, switching at |cos | = 10-6  two decades above the 10-8 guard be-
low which the generic fallback would engage, so that fallback is unreachable
from the pitch program. The two branches agree analytically; they dier
only in rounding, and the direct branch is taken wherever it reproduces the
pre-existing construction bit for bit. Note that equation (23.6) carries the
sign of cos : the   90 limit is -h^ I from below and +h^ I from above, so a program that crosses the vertical rather than departing it is a genuine 180
roll reversal, not a removable singularity.

23.3.4 Staging and jettison state remap
At a torque-free separation the composite center of mass jumps discretely
from body station cBold (the full stack) to cnBew (the retained stack), both given
by the closed-form composition of Chapter 19. The tracked translational state is the state of the composite CG, a material point of the retained body, so it is remapped by (FR-10)

rnIew = rI + CBI cB,

vnIew = vI + I Ṫ CBI cB ,

(23.7)

with cB = cnBew - coBld and  unchanged (a torque-free separation exerts no
angular impulse). Momentum conservation across the split is a consequence
of the rigid-body decomposition rather than an added model: with each
body's CG velocity vkI = vI + I Ṫ (CBI (ckB - cBold)), the mass-weighted CG osets sum to zero, so the summed linear momentum equals m vI exactly, and the summed angular momentum about the composite CG equals I 
exactly by the parallel-axis theorem that the composition itself applies. This
is the content of exit criterion 5.

23.4 Discretization and implementation
Implementation notes:

153

1. Modules and traceability. The pure geometry (equations (23.3)
(23.7)) lives in cpp/src/models/vehicle6dof.cpp, whose comments echo the equation labels; run_vehicle in cpp/src/run.cpp composes it with the model modules and echoes eq:vehicle6dof:state and eq:vehicle6dof:transaccel.

2. Control cycle and zero-order hold. At each cycle the run res due
sequence entries, composes the attached stack in the xed FR-10 body order (xed bodies, then one settled slug per tank, so the wet mass is a stable same-order sum), forms the commanded attitude, sets the zero-order-hold context, logs the decimated groups, then advances the RK4 translational step (when released), depletes the tanks at the held throttle, and advances the engine states.

3. Mass properties. The composite mass, CG, and inertia and their
time derivatives are the closed forms of Chapter 19; the propulsion mass ow is positive consumption negated into the signed tank depletion rate.

Events. 4.

Pad release, ignition, cuto, staging, jettison, orbit-insertion

(osculating perigee rising through the target), and the EarthMoon

SOI transition are located at control-cycle boundaries; a terminate

action stops the run and is logged as an event.

Determinism. 5.

Single-threaded, xed evaluation and summation or-

der, no allocation inside the RHS; the SRLOG v1.1 truth (real qŸ, ),

forces, mass, and env groups make the run bit-reproducible and its

force decomposition inspectable (FR-16).

This chapter relies on Vallado [57] for the geodetic-to-ECEF forward transform, on Markley and Crassidis [35] for the attitude construction, on Battin [5] for the two-body osculating-element relations behind the orbit-insertion condition, and on NIMA TR8350.2 [42] for the WGS84 reference ellipsoid. Chapter 24
Sensors: Inertial Measurement Unit
24.1 Purpose
This chapter species the FR-23 IMU sensor model: a triad of rate gyros
and a triad of accelerometers that emit accumulated increments  an an-
gular increment  and a velocity increment v per sample interval 
corrupted by a deterministic, seeded error chain comprising turn-on bias, rst-order GaussMarkov in-run bias, scale factor, small-angle misalignment, angular/velocity random walk, and quantization. Increments rather than point-sampled rates are the industry-standard strapdown interface (Titterton and Weston [56]; Savage [52]): the sensor integrates the true angular rate and specic force across the interval, so intra-interval motion (coning, sculling) is preserved in the signal handed to the navigation algorithms of Chapters 28 and 29 instead of being aliased away. The chapter also derives the Allan-variance identication machinery  the overlapping Allan deviation, the white-noise and bias-instability signatures, and the recovery
procedure  that Phase 6 exit criterion 1 gates: a 104 s static record must return the congured ARW and bias-instability coecients to within ḟ10 %.
24.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Sample schedule. The IMU emits one increment pair per GNC major
cycle (decision D-5): the sample interval is exactly the control period,
157

ts = Tc, and sample boundaries coincide with cycle boundaries, on
which the integrator is already forced to terminate. Faster-than-cycle IMU output is deliberately out of scope for v1.
2. Rigid mount at the center of mass. The sensor triads sit at the
composite center of mass with a xed body-frame orientation. The
size eect (lever-arm acceleration  Ṫ ( Ṫ r) +  Ṫ r at an o-CG station r) is excluded; its magnitude is bounded by 2 r +   r, e.g.  2Ṫ10-2 m s-2 for r = 0.5 m at  = 0.2 rad s-1, and a conguration
placing the IMU far o-CG on a tumbling vehicle is outside this model's domain.
3. Static error coecients. Scale factor, misalignment, and the noise
coecients are constant over a run: no temperature, g-sensitivity, or vibration rectication dependence. These belong to a higher-delity sensor tier, not v1 (PRD Non-Goals discipline).
4. GaussMarkov in-run bias. The in-run bias is a rst-order Gauss
Markov (exponentially correlated) process, held constant across each
sample interval (zero-order hold). The hold is valid for ts  c;
the per-interval error it commits relative to the continuous process is
O(ts/c) of the bias increment and is negligible for the supported regime ts  1 s, c  10 s.
5. No rate random walk. FR-23 names ARW/VRW, bias states, scale
factor, misalignment, and quantization; a rate-random-walk term is deliberately absent. Consequently the model's Allan deviation has no rising right-hand branch and no interior minimum; the bias-instability identication of Section 24.3.3 therefore evaluates the Allan deviation at the analytically known GaussMarkov peak abscissa rather than searching for a global minimum.
Domain of validity: any trajectory the core can propagate, with ts  c
(both gyro and accelerometer correlation times) and quadrature delity per the bound of equation (24.4). Out-of-domain congurations (non-positive
ts, c  0, negative noise densities or quanta) are rejected by the FR-15
conguration validator before the run starts; inside the deterministic loop the
model is a total function that never throws. All quantities are SI (rad, m s-1);
customary data-sheet units enter only through the documented conversions after equation (24.10).

24.3.4 Recovery procedure (exit criterion 1)
The identication test propagates a static truth trajectory (B  0, f B  0) for T = 104 s at a sample interval ts chosen so that m ts = 1 s is representable with integer m (e.g. ts = 0.01 s, m = 100), with a xed seed.
Per axis and per instrument:

163

1. Compute ^( ) from equation (24.12) on an octave grid  = 2j ts
restricted to   T /10, plus the two anchor points  = 1 s and  =   = 1.8926 c (the congured c is an input to the recovery, which
re-identies the noise magnitudes).

2. Recover the random-walk coecient at the one-second anchor by subtracting the two known model contributions in quadrature:

N^ = ^2(1 s) - G2 M(1 s) - Q2 (1 s),

(24.20)

with G2 M(Ṗ) from equation (24.15) at the congured (GM, c) and Q2 (Ṗ) from equation (24.19).

3. Recover the bias instability at the peak anchor by subtracting the recovered white-noise term and inverting equation (24.17):

B^ = 1 0.664282

(24.21)

4. Gate |N^ /N - 1|  0.10 and |B^/B - 1|  0.10.
The estimator dispersion supports the ḟ10 % gate: at  = 1 s the record holds  T /(2 ) = 5000 independent second dierences (relative ADEV scatter well under 2 %), and at   with the reference preset c = 20 s (  = 37.9 s) about T /(2 )  132 (scatter  6 %). Correlation times much beyond 50 s push   into the poorly estimated tail of a 104 s record and are excluded
from the gate scenario (not from the model). The committed test is seeded
and deterministic, so the gate is bit-stable across reruns (D-10).

24.4 Discretization and implementation
Binding implementation notes for the Phase 6 module:
1. Module and traceability. The model is a core-side ISensor (FR-
23) sampled once per major cycle. The implementing source echoes
the labels eq:imu:dtheta, eq:imu:gyro, eq:imu:accel, eq:imu:gm, eq:imu:arw, eq:imu:quant verbatim in comments and adds this chap-
ter's manifest entry.
2. Evaluation order per sample, normative. (1) advance the gyro
and accelerometer GaussMarkov states by equation (24.9); (2) form

164

the bracketed values of equations (24.5) and (24.6) from the accumulated truth increments; (3) apply the quantizer of equation (24.11). Truth accumulation (equation (24.3)) runs inside the propagation loop as steps are accepted; the accumulator resets to zero at each sample boundary.
3. Seeded stream and draw schedule, normative. All draws come
from the named stream sensors.imu (D-9) through the core NormalSampler. Initialization consumes, in order: gyro turn-on bias (x, y, z), gyro GaussMarkov initial state (x, y, z), accelerometer turn-on bias (x, y, z), accelerometer GaussMarkov initial state (x, y, z). Each sample consumes, in order: gyro GaussMarkov drive (x, y, z), gyro ARW (x, y, z), accelerometer GaussMarkov drive (x, y, z), accelerometer VRW (x, y, z).
Draws are unconditional  a zero coecient multiplies a drawn normal by zero rather than skipping the draw  so the stream schedule is independent of which error terms are enabled and every conguration of one consumer leaves all other streams untouched.
4. Logged channels. Measured increments land in the reserved sensors.*
group (FR-16) with unit-suxed names; the true GaussMarkov bias states are logged alongside as truth-side diagnostics so the Chapter 29 consistency evaluation can form full-state estimation errors without access to core internals.
5. Determinism. Fixed evaluation order, no allocation in the sample
path, one carry state per axis per instrument (equation (24.11))  the only sensor state besides the GaussMarkov biases; identical seeds reproduce identical increment streams bit-for-bit (D-10, exit criterion 1's bit-identity clause).
24.5 Validation evidence
The module implementing this chapter is cpp/src/sensors/imu.cpp. The
full error chain of equations (24.5)(24.11) and the Allan identication of Section 24.3.4 have landed, so every gate this chapter species now appears in the tables below with a machine-checked test identier. The zero-error increments remain the model's zero-coecient special case: each error stage degenerates to an exact identity, which is itself asserted rather than assumed.
Three items specied by this chapter remain outstanding and are recorded here rather than tabled, so the evidence tables state only evidence that exists:

A note on equation (24.19), for anyone writing a quantization-specic
Allan gate: the Q( ) = q/(2 ) signature assumes the carried residual is
white sample to sample, which the carry of equation (24.11) makes true only when the input is dithered at or above roughly one quantum. Below that
the residual is correlated over  q/in samples and the measured ADEV falls
below this formula at short cluster times  a property of the model, not a defect. The committed Allan gate runs with the quantizer disabled, so the term is exactly zero there.
24.6 References
The increment interface and strapdown error taxonomy follow Titterton and Weston [56] and Savage [52]; the Allan variance denitions, noise-signature table (white, quantization, bias-instability relation (24.17)), and test procedure follow IEEE Std 952 [25] and Riley [51], with the underlying statistic due to Allan [1]. The exact GaussMarkov discretization (24.9) is standard (Maybeck [36]); the GaussMarkov Allan variance (24.15) is derived above from the process autocorrelation. Full bibliographic details appear in the bibliography.

Chapter 25
Sensors: Star Tracker and Sun Sensor

25.1 Purpose
This chapter species the FR-23 optical attitude sensors: a star tracker that emits a small-angle-corrupted attitude quaternion with Sun/body exclusion and slew-rate gating, and a sun sensor that emits a noisy unit vector toward
velocity- the apparent Sun. It also denes, once for the whole project, the aberration correction that FR-23 applies to every optical truth direction
(star tracker, sun sensor, and the camera hook of Chapter 27): the project's light-time/aberration policy is that dynamics use geometric ephemeris positions (Chapter 6), while optical sensor truth adds the velocity aberration of
Section 25.3.1  a  20.5 eect at Earth's heliocentric orbital speed, an or-
der of magnitude above an arcsecond-class star-tracker error budget  with the residual light-time eects bounded in Section 25.2. Phase 6 exit criterion 9 gates an independent recomputation of the stated aberration formula
to < 1 mas, and exit criterion 1 gates the star-tracker error statistics inside
two-sided 95 % chi-square bounds over 1,000 draws, so every convention here  frames, sign, normalization, composition order  is stated exactly.

25.2 Assumptions and domain of validity

Assumptions:

1. Light-time/aberration policy (FR-23). Source directions are com-

geometric puted from

(instantaneous) ephemeris positions and then

170

corrected for velocity (stellar) aberration only. The neglected planetaryaberration term  the source's own motion during the light time 
displaces the apparent Sun by  11 mas (solar barycentric velocity  16 m s-1 acting over 499 s) and a Moon-xed landmark seen from 4 Ṫ 108 m by  0.7 (lunar orbital velocity  1 km s-1 over 1.3 s);
both are below the arcsecond-class sensor noise this suite targets, and both bounds scale linearly with source velocity and light time for other geometries.
2. First-order aberration. The rst-order formula of equation (25.2) is
used, not the exact special-relativistic form; the dierence is (2/4) sin 2+ O(3) in apparent angle ( the sourcevelocity angle), at most 0.52 mas at  = 10-4 (v = 30 km s-1)  below every stated gate.
3. Stars at innity. Catalog directions are truth by construction; par-
allax is not modeled (the simulator has no star catalog  the tracker abstraction below absorbs it).
4. Narrow-eld tracker abstraction. The star tracker is modeled at
the attitude level: matching, centroiding, and the star eld itself are abstracted into a body-frame small-angle error with congured peraxis standard deviations (about-boresight typically the largest). The aberration of the observed star eld enters as the rigid eld rotation of equation (25.4); the residual dierential aberration across the eld
of view is O(2) for FOV half-angle   below 1 for   10 at  = 10-4  and is absorbed in the congured noise.
5. Exclusion angles as conguration. Exclusion gating compares the
boresight to the apparent direction of each congured excluded body against a congured half-angle per body; the angle is understood to include the body's angular radius plus stray-light margin. The model does not compute limb geometry for the tracker.
Domain of validity:  = vobs /c  10-3 (the rst-order error bound above grows as 2), congured error sigmas  10-2 rad (the small-angle statistics of Section 25.3.4 degrade as O(2) beyond that), and exclusion/FOV half-angles in (0, /2). Out-of-domain congurations are rejected by the
FR-15 validator; the in-loop model is a total function and never throws. Milliarcsecond-grade astrometry (relativistic light deection, parallax, proper motion) is explicitly out of scope.

25.3 Derivation

25.3.1 Velocity aberration

Let u^I be the geometric unit direction from the observer to the source, re-

barycentric composition; using the planet-relative velocity alone would omit
the dominant  30 km s-1 annual term. The apparent direction is, to rst order in  (Kaplan [29]),
