25.4 Discretization and implementation
Binding implementation notes for the Phase 6 modules:
1. Modules and traceability. Star tracker and sun sensor are core-
side ISensor modules sampled on the major-cycle schedule (D-5), on the named streams sensors.st and sensors.sun respectively (D-9). Source comments echo the labels eq:optical:aberration, eq:optical:rho,

175

eq:optical:qab, eq:optical:stmodel, eq:optical:noiseq, and eq:optical:sunsensor
verbatim; the aberration of equation (25.2) is one shared core function used by both sensors and by the camera hook (Chapter 27)  a single code path is what makes exit criterion 9 a single gate.
2. Draw schedule, normative. Star tracker: three normals per sample
(1, 2, 3). Sun sensor: three normals per sample (1, 2, 3). Uncon-
ditional draws, per the Chapter 24 rule.
3. Quaternion output. Scalar-rst per Table 1.2; the emitted quater-
nion is normalized after the product (25.6) (the factors are unit to
not rounding; the explicit normalization pins the invariant) and is
sign-canonicalized  consumers own the double cover, as does the extraction (25.11).
4. Ephemeris inputs.  per equation (25.1) from the same DE440 chain
the dynamics use; for a Mars- or Moon-centered run the central-body barycentric velocity replaces the Earth chain. No sensor code reads
the clock or any state outside GncInput-visible truth supplied by the
core scheduler.
5. Logged channels. Measurement, validity ag, and the per-sample
apparent-direction inputs land in sensors.st.* / sensors.sun.* with
unit-suxed names, at the sensor rate.
25.5 Validation evidence The modules implementing this chapter are cpp/src/sensors/optical.cpp
(both sensors and the shared aberration function).

What the criterion-9 tolerance is, and what it is not. The 1 mas

requirement gure is the

exit criterion 9 states, not a measure of what the

implementation achieves and not a physical error budget. Both sides of the

comparison evaluate the same normative equation (25.2), so the residual is

an arithmetic disagreement between two transcriptions, and the measured
worst value is 4.726 Ṫ 10-8 mas  some 2.1 Ṫ 107 times inside the criterion's

own gure. Setting the assertion at the requirement rather than near the

achievable agreement had a consequence worth stating plainly: a reference

mutation that drops the transverse projection from equation (25.2) (writing
u +  for u +  - (u Ṗ )u, a change at second order only) moves the residual to 0.4696 mas on this xture and therefore passed a 1 mas gate. It passed

180

because that tolerance was loose relative to the achievable agreement, not
because 1 mas is forced by anything physical. The assertion has accordingly been tightened, which is the remediation recorded under KNOWN-ISSUE-P6-2: the committed constant now reads ABERRATION_TOL_MAS = 1e-5, retaining 211.6Ṫ headroom over the measured residual while rejecting the droptransverse mutation by a factor of about 4.7 Ṫ 104. The criterion's own 1 mas
gure is asserted alongside it, so the suite states the requirement it meets and not only the tighter bound it is held to.
Tightening the tolerance is necessary but not sucient, because the residual is an angular separation and so is invariant under a rotation applied to both of its arguments. Two further changes make the gate sensitive to the attitude convention. The reference side now rotates through
tests/refs/quaternions.quat_to_dcm: the core's own DCM previously
appeared on both sides of the separation and cancelled exactly, so no convention error could reach the residual. The xture's commanded attitude
was also moved o the body +Z axis, because the earlier slew held qw = 0 for the whole run, and there C - CT = -4qw [qv]Ṫ vanishes identically  a
transposed convention was invisible by geometry regardless of which imple-
mentation supplied the DCM. The o-axis slew carries |qw| up to 0.060 and max|C-CT | up to 0.18; test_aberration_fixture_can_see_an_attitude_convention_error
pins that asymmetry so the xture cannot drift back into the blind plane. Distinct from the tolerance, and genuinely a modelling choice rather than
a gate weakness: this chapter declares the rst-order form (25.2) normative,
and the gap to the exact relativistic form is 0.51 mas at Earth's mean heliocentric speed and 0.81 mas once low-Earth-orbit speed is added. Criterion 9
recomputes the rst-order form on both sides deliberately; gating the core against the exact form would report a deliberate modelling decision as an implementation error. That gap is measured, and asserted against assump-
tion 2's own bound, by test_first_order_versus_exact_gap_is_recorded,
which is recorded as non-normative for exactly this reason. Outstanding, recorded rather than tabled:
 Attitude convention inside the criterion-9 gate. The refer-
ence side of test_aberration_matches_independent_reference ro-
tates its apparent direction into the body frame with the core's own
quat_to_dcm, and the residual is an angular separation, which is invari-
ant under a rotation common to both sides. The core DCM therefore cancels exactly and no error in it could be detected there. An indepen-
dently validated implementation exists at tests/refs/quaternions.py
and is already used by the Chapter 27 pixel gate; substituting it
181

closes the hole. The convention is not unpinned in the project 

test_rotation_bindings_match_goldens gates that same binding against

here the Chapter 4 goldens to 10-15 per element  but it is not pinned

,

and the criterion-9 row should not be read as evidence for it.

The boundary sweeps of equations (25.8) and (25.10) were outstanding here until the three gating rows above were committed, and the reason they went uncommitted for as long as they did is worth recording. The exclusion terms were reachable in principle from the start, but no xture reached them: the mission that congured both radii carried an invalid ephemeris, so the guard above the exclusion block rejected every sample before them, and the only mission with a valid ephemeris set both radii to zero. The result was a validity ag written on every sample of every run whose computation had never executed, which a systematic coverage measurement found and no amount of assertion counting would have
(docs/review/phase6_coverage_audit.md, nding C-1). The rows above
are placed in the C++ tier so the gate is also inside the reach of the sanitizer and warnings-as-errors legs, and each is recorded as failing under an inver-
sion, a scaled radius, and a ipped reference direction in docs/review/phase6_coverage_closure.md.
A scope note on equation (25.8): the implemented exclusion set is the Sun and the central body, each with its own congured half-angle. The general "each congured excluded body" form requires a congured third-body table that the sensor layer does not yet receive; the single-code-path treatment of apparent directions is unaected, since both implemented exclusions run through equation (25.2).

25.6 References
The aberration treatment follows the IAU-resolution exposition of Kaplan [29] (velocity aberration and its rst-order form), restricted per the FR-23 policy to the stellar-aberration term; the attitude-measurement abstraction and quaternion conventions follow Markley and Crassidis [35], transcribed to the project convention of Chapter 1 as noted at equation (25.6). Full bibliographic details appear in the bibliography.

182

Chapter 26
Sensors: External Nav Fix and Altimeter
26.1 Purpose
external nav x This chapter species the two radio-class FR-23 sensors. The
is the project's generalization of GNSS (assumption A-6): an abstract service that delivers position and velocity xes in the GCRF with congurable Gaussian errors, so the same sensor stands in for GPS, a future LNSS-class lunar service, or ground-based radiometric tracking without re-architecting. The
altimeter delivers a scalar geodetic-altitude measurement over the central
body's reference ellipsoid with a per-run bias and white noise. Both feed the Chapter 29 reference EKF as aiding updates, and both are gated by Phase 6 exit criterion 6: error statistics inside two-sided 95 % chi-square bounds over 1,000 seeded draws, with the exact statistic dened in Section 26.3.3.
26.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Fix-level abstraction. The nav x models the output of an external
navigation service, not its measurements: no pseudoranges, constellation geometry, dilution of precision, clock states, or atmospheric delays. Error anisotropy that a real service exhibits (e.g. vertical ination) is expressible through the per-axis sigmas; error correlation with geometry is not, and analyses that depend on it are outside this model's domain.
183

GCRF axes. 2.

Fix errors are drawn per GCRF axis. A service whose

natural error frame is local (east/north/up) is approximated by choos-

ing equivalent GCRF sigmas; the dierence matters only for strongly

anisotropic congurations.

3. Optional correlated component. A rst-order GaussMarkov error
component exists as an option on both the position and the velocity x (Section 26.3.1), defaulted o. It models slowly varying service biases (ephemeris/clock residuals). When enabled, the chi-square gate of Section 26.3.3 applies only to the white part (the gate scenario disables the correlated part); a separate deterministic test pins the recursion.

4. Altimeter over the reference ellipsoid. The altimeter measures
geodetic altitude over the central body's reference ellipsoid exactly as the environment models do (Chapter 16): the Bowring two-pass conversion of Chapter 13, equation (13.5), applied to the Earth-xed (or planet-xed) truth position via the Chapter 5 rotation. Terrain, tides, and geoid undulation are not modeled  the instrument is a radar altimeter over the ellipsoid, and any scenario needing terrain-relative altitude is out of scope.

No latency. 5.

Fixes apply at their sample instant; transport and pro-

cessing latency for realism studies is provided generically by the FR-25
latency_cycles mechanism (Chapter 28), not duplicated per sensor.

Domain of validity: any state the core can propagate; the altimeter additionally requires the truth position inside its congured operating band
h  [hmin, hmax] (outside it the sample is emitted with valid = false, the ag
semantics of Chapter 25) and outside the Bowring conversion's polar-axis neighborhood only in the sense documented in Chapter 13. Non-positive
sigmas, c  0, or hmin  hmax are rejected by the FR-15 validator; the
in-loop model never throws.

With h(r) the geodetic altitude of the truth position over the central body's reference ellipsoid  the planet-xed position CIE rI (Chapter 5) put through the Bowring two-pass conversion of equation (13.5) with the body's (a, 1/f ); for a spherical body (f = 0) the conversion degenerates exactly to h = r-a

26.4 Discretization and implementation
Binding implementation notes for the Phase 6 modules:
1. Modules and traceability. Both sensors are core-side ISensor mod-
ules on the named streams sensors.navfix and sensors.alt (D-9). Source comments echo eq:radio:fix, eq:radio:gm, eq:radio:alt, and eq:radio:chi2 verbatim.
2. Draw schedule, normative. Nav x, per sample and in order: po-
sition GaussMarkov drive (x, y, z) if enabled, velocity GaussMarkov drive (x, y, z) if enabled, position white (x, y, z), velocity white (x, y, z).
Enabling a GaussMarkov component also consumes its stationaryinitialization draws at run start (position then velocity). Altimeter: turn-on bias (one draw at run start), then one white draw per sample. Within a xed conguration the schedule is unconditional; enabling or disabling the optional components is a conguration change and lands in the resolved cong hash (FR-15), which is the reproducibility anchor.
3. Geodetic reuse. The altimeter calls the same core geodetic-altitude
function the atmosphere and environment models use (Chapters 13,

186

16)  no second conversion path; its accuracy budget (sub-millimetre in-domain) is inherited and already documented there.
4. Logged channels. Measurements and ags land under sensors.navfix.*
and sensors.alt.* with unit-suxed names at the sensor rate.

of the

implementation: geodetic_altitude() validates 1/f > 1 and rejects zero

attening outright rather than returning the limit. The altimeter there-
fore branches explicitly on a spherical central body and evaluates r - a

in closed form, which additionally needs no body-xed rotation. The two

branches agree in the limit and the single-conversion-path intent of imple-

mentation note 3 is preserved for every ellipsoidal body; the at statement

above should be read as "degenerates to" in the mathematical sense only.

Chapter 27
Camera Hook: Pose, Intrinsics, and Landmark Projection

27.1 Purpose

hook This chapter species the FR-23 camera

: a sensor that emits geometric

truth for oine external rendering and optical-navigation research  the

camera pose, the pinhole intrinsics, the list of visible bodies, the apparent

no Sun vector, and optional landmark pixel projections  with

in-core ren-

no dering and

noise. It is the substrate for the world-model and AI/ML

navigation work of the later phases: an external renderer or a learned per-

ception model consumes the emitted pose stream and produces images or

measurements, while the core remains small and deterministic. Everything
bit-exactly emitted is truth: Phase 6 exit criterion 7 gates the pose channels
against the truth channels, and gates the landmark projections against an independent NumPy pinhole script to < 10-6 pixels  which is why every

frame, axis, and pixel convention in this chapter is stated exactly. The crite-
rion also names the intrinsics, which the sensors.camera record layout does

not carry; that clause is uncovered, and Section 27.5 records why. Direc-

tion outputs carry the FR-23 velocity-aberration correction of Chapter 25,

applied through the same shared code path.

27.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Ideal pinhole. No lens distortion, defocus, rolling shutter, or expo-

191

sure model: projection is the exact central projection of equation (27.6) (Hartley and Zisserman [23]). Distortion belongs to the external renderer or perception model, not the truth hook.

2. Rigid mount, CG-relative. The camera is rigidly mounted at the congured body-frame oset rcBam relative to the composite center of mass (the point whose state the truth channels carry), with xed ori-
entation qŸb2c. Center-of-mass travel during propellant depletion (Chap-
ter 19) is therefore not re-projected onto the mount: for a station-xed
physical camera the neglected oset is bounded by the vehicle's CG
travel (centimetres to a metre on the DX-3 starter eet)  immaterial
at orbital target ranges, and zero for the rigid post-burn spacecraft this
hook targets.

3. Spherical occluders. Visibility against a body uses its mean spher-
ical radius (IAU values per Archinal et al. [2], as congured); terrain and oblateness are not modeled in the occlusion tests. Near-limb landmarks within the oblateness band of the true gure may be misclassied; scenarios that care sit the landmark away from the limb.

4. Light-time policy. Per FR-23 and Chapter 25: geometric ephemeris

directions positions, velocity aberration on emitted

(landmark projec-

tions and the Sun vector), residual light-time eects bounded there.

pose The emitted

is geometric truth and is not aberrated  aberra-

tion is a property of arriving light, not of the platform state.

5. Landmarks are body-xed points. A landmark is a congured
position T in a target body's body-xed frame (Moon principal-axis,
Mars-xed, or Earth-xed frames of Chapter 5); it rotates rigidly with
the body.

Domain of validity: any propagatable state; projections are dened for
landmarks strictly in front of the camera (Z C > 0, enforced by the visibility
ag rather than by exception); the model is a total, noise-free, draw-free
function inside the loop and never throws. Congurations with fx, fy  0,
non-positive image dimensions, or a landmark on an uncongured body are
rejected by the FR-15 validator.

27.3 Derivation

27.3.1 Pose and frame chain
The camera frame C follows the standard computer-vision convention (Hartley and Zisserman [23]): +Z C along the boresight (out of the camera, toward the scene), +X C toward increasing image column (u, right), +Y C toward increasing image row (v, down)  a right-handed triad. The chain from
inertial to camera is

qŸi2c = qŸi2b  qŸb2c,

rcIam = rI + CIB(qŸi2b)T rcBam,

(27.1)

with rI , qŸi2b the truth state (composition per equation (1.8)). The emitted pose channels are rI and qŸi2b themselves, byte-identical to the truth group

(exit criterion 7).

record The constants qŸb2c, rcBam, and the intrinsics are not

channels 

they do not vary sample to sample, so repeating them per record would be
waste  but they are echoed once in the log header, at gnc.camera,

as of SRLOG v1.3. A consumer therefore composes equation (27.1) and

the intrinsic matrix equation (27.2) from the log alone, without the mission
oine exter- le. That is what FR-23 needs: the hook exists to feed an nal renderer, and the pose channels carry the vehicle state rather than the

camera's, so without the echo a renderer could neither place the camera nor

build its projection matrix from the le. The header rule that oats never

appear there is preserved by carrying each double as its IEEE-754 binary64

bit pattern in sixteen hex digits, an encoding that is exact and whose writer

runs no oat formatter; docs/formats/srlog_v1.md section 3 is normative

positions for it. Landmark

remain resolved-conguration data: the count L

already rides in the record dtype, and echoing a xture-scale landmark table

would add kilobytes to every camera header.

An earlier revision of this chapter asserted this echo while no implemen-

tation existed  veried against a run at the time, no intrinsic, extrinsic, or

landmark value appeared anywhere in the header. That gap was the direct

cause of exit criterion 7's uncovered intrinsics clause; the echo described here
is the closure, and test_camera_intrinsics_echo_reproduces_logged_pixels

gates it.

27.4 Discretization and implementation

Binding implementation notes for the Phase 6 module:

1. Module and traceability. The camera hook is a core-side ISensor no on the major-cycle schedule (D-5) with PRNG stream  it is noise-
free truth and consumes no draws. Source comments echo eq:camera:pose,
eq:camera:K, eq:camera:landmark, eq:camera:apparent, eq:camera:proj,
and eq:camera:occlusion verbatim.

2. Bit-exact pose emission. The pose channels are copies of the same

doubles the truth writer receives  not recomputed values  so exit

pose criterion 7's

bit-exactness clause is satised by construction. The

intrinsics and the extrinsics are taken from the resolved congura-

tion verbatim, without recomputation, but they are not written to
the record stream: they are conguration, and the sensors.camera

layout below carries no channel for them. The criterion's intrinsics

clause is uncovered for that reason; see the discussion following the

evidence table.

3. Evaluation order. Per sample: pose copy; per landmark: equa-
tions (27.3)(27.6), then the four visibility tests in the stated order with short-circuit evaluation (the projection values are logged even when a later test fails, with the ag false  consumers lter on the ag); then the visible-bodies list; then the Sun vector.

4. Cross-check tolerance. The < 10-6 pixel gate against the inde-
pendent NumPy script absorbs double-rounding-order dierences be-
tween the core and NumPy ( 10-16 relative on kilo-pixel coordinates  10-13 pixels) with six orders of margin; the gate tolerance is set by
the reproduction delity this chapter's conventions must support, not
by oating-point noise.

5. Logged channels. Everything lands under sensors.cam.* with unit-
suxed names: pose, per-landmark (u, v, visible), per-body visibility,
Sun vector.

and intrinsics hook's pose

to equal the truth channels bit-exactly. Read

px_uv to the same 10-6 pixel tolerance as the pixel clause. This is not the

earlier conguration-against-conguration comparison: the echoed constants

are load-bearing, so a header echo that disagreed with the constants the hook

projected through fails the gate by a wide margin. The mutation evidence

is tabulated with the test.

The following remains outstanding:

 Aberration consistency across hooks. Pairing the camera Sun vec-
tor of equation (27.9) against the sun-sensor direction of Chapter 25 on one run, conrming both resolve the same apparent direction through the shared aberration path. No committed test compares the two.

Scope of the implemented hook. Landmarks are body-xed points on

central the

body, which is the surface-relative optical-navigation case this

hook targets and is served exactly by the central-body-xed rotation the

environment model already composes for the dynamics. Landmarks on a

third body, and with them the multi-body occlusion test of equation (27.8),

require a congured body table the sensor layer does not yet receive; the

near-side test of equation (27.7) is exact for a spherical central body and a

surface landmark, so self-occlusion is handled without it. Note also that a

at landmark placed

the body center is degenerate for that test, whose dot

200

Logged channels versus emitted quantities. Implementation note 5
lists the visible-bodies list and the Sun vector among the logged channels,
but the normative sensors.camera record layout carries ts, r, qŸi2b, and the 2L interleaved pixel coordinates only. The Sun vector of equation (27.9) is
computed through the shared aberration path and exposed to in-process consumers, and the per-landmark visibility ags likewise; extending the record to carry them would be a log-format change, which this implementation deliberately does not make. The intrinsics are a dierent case: they are constants rather than per-sample quantities, so they are not record channels either, but v1.3 echoes them once in the header (Section 27.3.1) rather than leaving them in the resolved conguration alone. Exit criterion 7 gates the pose, the intrinsics, and the landmark pixels; the record stream carries the rst and the third, the header echo carries the second, and all three clauses are gated.

The pinhole model, intrinsics matrix, and image-coordinate conventions follow Hartley and Zisserman [23]; body radii and rotational elements follow Archinal et al. [2] through the frames machinery of Chapter 5; the aberration correction is specied once in Chapter 25 after Kaplan [29]. Full bibliographic details appear in the bibliography.

Chapter 28
Built-in Reference GNC Components

28.1 Purpose

This chapter species the built-in C++ reference components behind the

FR-25 plugin interface: (a) a quaternion-error PD attitude controller, (b)

a dead-reckoning attitude navigator driven by the Chapter 24 gyro incre-

ments, and (c) the ascent pitch-program guidance  the Phase 4 open-
loop pitch program of Chapter 23 re-expressed as an IGncComponent so

the same ascent ies under the GNC stack (Phase 6 exit criterion 10). It

also pins the plugin-boundary semantics every component, built-in or user-

supplied, shares: zero-order-hold commands over the major cycle (D-5), the

latency_cycles shift (exit criterion 8), and the oracle truth-injection ag

reference (exit criterion 5). These components are

implementations: delib-

erately simple, exactly specied, and reproducible in a few lines of Python

 exit criterion 2 requires a Python reimplementation of the PD controller
to match the C++ torques to < 10-9 N m, so every branch and operation

order in Section 28.3.3 is normative.

28.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Cycle-synchronous execution. Components run once per major
cycle on the D-5 schedule; all inputs are the sensor samples of that cycle and all outputs are held (zero-order hold) across the next application

202

interval. No component sees intra-cycle states.

2. No truth in GncInput. Components consume only sensor outputs,

their own state, and conguration. The scenario-level oracle: true

and debug ag injects truth into GncInput

stamps the log header, so

an oracle run is identiable from its header alone (exit criterion 5); the

reference components themselves never read the oracle elds.

3. Diagonal gains, per-axis saturation. The PD controller uses pos-
itive per-axis gain vectors and clamps each torque axis independently (equation (28.11)); a saturated command is direction-distorted, which is the standard, simplest behavior and is stated rather than hidden.

4. Dead reckoning is uncompensated. The dead-reckoning navigator
applies no bias compensation and no coning correction; its drift is exactly the integrated gyro error plus the bounded single-sample noncommutativity residual of equation (28.14). It exists as the minimal reference navigator and as the mechanization core the Chapter 29 lter shares.

5. Guidance restates Phase 4 math. The ascent guidance reuses the
pitch-program geometry of Chapter 23 (equations (23.4) and (23.5)) unchanged; this chapter adds only its packaging as a component and the commanded-rate convention.

Domain of validity: attitude-regulation regimes with per-cycle error rota-
tions far from the ḟ antipode (the sign branch of equation (28.10) handles the double cover; exactly at qw = 0, 180 error, the branch picks s = +1
deterministically and the controller still converges, though the commanded direction at that single point is convention, not physics). Gains are the user's stability responsibility: the PD law is globally stabilizing for a rigid body with pure torque actuation and positive gains (Wie [60]), but actuator saturation, latency, and exible dynamics can destabilize aggressive tunings  the simulator reports what the conguration does, per the project's nosilent-correction rule (DX-2).

28.3 Derivation
28.3.1 Plugin-boundary semantics
Let Tc be the control period and tk = k Tc the cycle boundaries. At cycle k the scheduler samples sensors, calls each congured component's update,

203

composes the stack's nal actuator command vector uk (torque and/or gim-
bal/throttle commands, per the actuator suite of Chapter 21), and applies it
as a zero-order hold. With the congured latency L = latency_cycles  0,
the command applied over [tk, tk+1) is

ukapplied =

uk-L, uneutral,

k  L, k < L,

(28.1)

where the neutral command is zero torque, zero gimbal deection, and throt-

tle hold at the sequence-commanded value. The shift applies once, at the

GNC-to-plant boundary, not per component. What holds by construction is

a statement about the FIFO alone: fed one command sequence, its output
is that sequence delayed by exactly  cycles with  neutral cycles prepended. That is what gnc_latency_fifo_semantics gates, in open loop, where the

input sequence is xed.

not It does

extend to the logged history of a run, and the distinction

is easy to lose. The loop is closed, so delaying the applied torque changes

the plant trajectory; from cycle 1 onward an L =  run and an L = 0

compute run see dierent states and therefore

dierent commands. Only

cycle 0 is comparable between the two runs, which is precisely the comparison
test_latency_two_cycles_shifts_application makes. Read as a claim about gnc.cmd, the L =  history is the L = 0 history delayed by  is false;

the criterion is veried at one cycle pair end to end, and generally only at

the FIFO. Closing the general case needs an open-loop assertion driving the

cycle with a recorded command sequence against a xed plant and asserting
uapplied[i + ] = ucomputed[i] for every i, including the drain at run end, where the last  computed commands are never applied and no committed

test looks. Both the computed and the applied commands are logged, which

is what makes the criterion checkable from the log at all.

28.3.2 Declared error-state layout
The nav.err channel records truth minus estimate in the estimator's own
state convention. Forming it needs two things: the true state, and a reading of what each slot of the estimator's state vector means. Only the component knows the second, and the natural arrangement  hand the component the truth state and let it subtract  is the one this interface deliberately avoids. It would place the true state in the hands of every estimator on every cycle whether or not the scenario enabled the oracle, contradicting the FR-24 requirement that truth is privileged and never visible to GNC plugins, and no signature can prevent an implementation from retaining what it is passed.

204

declares The dependency is therefore inverted. A component

the layout

of its state vector; the loop reads the state vector the component publishes

and performs the dierencing itself. What crosses the plugin boundary is a

description of the state vector, which carries no information about the world.
A layout is an ordered set of blocks {(qj , fj , oj )}, where qj names the true quantity the block is compared against, fj the form of the comparison, and oj the block's rst index. The blocks must tile [0, n) exactly for a state of dimension n: a gap would be logged as zero, and zero in an error channel

reads as no error rather than not known. A component that declares no
layout is written no nav.err channel at all, for the same reason.

For every quantity other than attitude the comparison is elementwise,
with x the published state vector and z the corresponding true quantity:

eo+i = zi - xo+i.

(28.2)

Attitude is why the form is declared rather than assumed. An attitude
error is a rotation dierence, not a subtraction of quaternion components,
and both the side on which it is composed and its parameterization are
conventions the estimator owns. Writing qŸest for the estimate read out of slots o . . . o + 3 (scalar-rst, D-7) and qŸtrue for the true attitude, the two
multiplicative forms are

qŸlocal = qŸest  qŸtrue, qŸglobal = qŸtrue  qŸest,

(28.3) (28.4)

the rst resolved in the estimated body frame and the second in the inertial
frame. Both are canonicalized to the +w hemisphere, since qŸ and -qŸ are the
same rotation and without the convention the four logged components could ip sign between neighbouring epochs for no physical reason. Equation (28.3) is exactly the multiplicative error the reference lter of Chapter 29 denes in (29.2), which is how that lter's declared layout reproduces its previous output unchanged.
Where the estimator's state carries a three-component attitude error in-
stead of the quaternion, the same qŸ is reduced by the small-angle relation

 = 2 sgn(qw) qv,

(28.5)

which is the reduction the consistency evaluator applies to compare an attitude error against the covariance it describes.
The two rotation-vector forms are not usable through a declared layout as the code currently stands, and the discrepancy is recorded here rather than

205

papered over. A rotation-vector attitude block is three slots wide, which is the width the layout validator tiles the state vector with, but the dierencing routine reads four quaternion slots at the block's oset. A layout that passes validation therefore cannot supply the fourth slot from within its own block: the read runs into the following block, or past the end of the state buer if the attitude block is last. Neither reading of the intent repairs it  a threeslot block carries no absolute attitude to dierence truth against, while a
four-slot one leaves a slot of nav.err unwritten, and nav.err is declared with nav.est's dimension, so that slot would log as zero, which this section
has just said an error channel must not do. Resolving it is a design decision with a log-format consequence. Neither built-in component selects either form  the reference lter of Chapter 29 declares equation (28.3) and the dead-reckoning navigator the additive form below  so no run reaches it today, but both are public API a plugin author can select. The evidence row below pins the arithmetic of (28.5) on a quaternion supplied directly, which is what the routine computes; it does not certify the layout path. See
docs/review/phase6_coverage_closure.md.
A fourth form serves an estimator that treats the four quaternion components as ordinary state entries, as the dead-reckoning navigator of Section 28.3.4 does. Its error is additive, with the true quaternion rst signaligned to the estimate's hemisphere:

eo+i = sgn(qŸtrue Ṗ qŸest) qtrue,i - qest,i, i = 0, . . . , 3,

(28.6)

where the sign convention takes sgn(0) = +1 so that an exactly orthogonal
pair is not ipped. Alignment is what keeps the additive dierence continuous across the double cover.
The loop dierences against the same published state vector it writes to
nav.est on that cycle, which makes the logged error provably the error of
the logged estimate rather than of a second, separately read state.

28.3.3 Quaternion-error PD attitude controller

Inputs per cycle: the commanded attitude and rate (qŸi2cmd, cCmMdD) from the guidance component, and the estimated attitude and rate (qŸ^i2b, ^ B ) from
the navigation component. The error quaternion is the attitude of the actual

body frame relative to the commanded frame, obtained from the composition

rule (1.8):

qŸ = qŸcmd2b = qŸi2cmd  q^Ÿi2b,

(28.7)

206

so qŸ = [1, 0] at zero error, and for small errors qv  /2 with  the rotation
vector from commanded to actual body frame. The rate error resolves the commanded rate into body axes through the error DCM,

err = ^ B - CCBMD(qŸ) cCmMdD,

(28.8)

with the DCM from equation (1.7). The commanded torque, componentwise
for i  {x, y, z} and with the shortest-path sign

s = +1, qw  0, -1, qw < 0,
is
i = - Kp,i s qv,i - Kd,i err,i,
followed by the per-axis clamp
i  min max(i, -max,i), max,i .

(28.9) (28.10) (28.11)

Normative arithmetic, for the exit-criterion-2 reproduction: the inputs are
used as received (no renormalization of qŸ); the Hamilton product (1.4) and
conjugate are evaluated in the project's scalar-rst component order; the
sign branch is exactly qw  0 (zero maps to +1); products and clamps are elementwise with the gains Kp,i > 0 (N m, per unit quaternion-vector component) and Kd,i > 0 (N m s rad-1). Because qv  /2, the small-error proportional stiness is Kp,i/2 per radian  the factor of two lives in the gain interpretation, not in the code. The s factor selects the shorter of the
two rotations representing the same error (quaternion double cover), which
removes the classical unwinding behavior; global asymptotic stability of the
law for a rigid body with positive-denite gains is the standard quaternion-
feedback result (Wie [60]; Markley and Crassidis [35]).

28.4 Discretization and implementation
Binding implementation notes for the Phase 6 modules:
1. Modules and traceability. Each component is a C++ IGncComponent
registered in the FR-25 static registry and selected by conguration string; Python subclasses enter through the pybind11 trampoline with
identical semantics. Source comments echo eq:gnc:deltaq, eq:gnc:pd, eq:gnc:sat, eq:gnc:werr, eq:gnc:exactrot, eq:gnc:drprop, and eq:gnc:cmdrate verbatim.
2. Statelessness inventory. The PD controller is stateless; the dead
reckoner's state is qŸ^; the guidance's state is the frozen basis and tables. All state is reset by Sim.reset (FR-24), which is what makes stepping
and batch runs bit-identical (exit criterion 4).

209

3. No draws, no clock, no allocation. Components consume no
PRNG streams and never read wall-clock time; the update path allocates nothing (D-10).
4. Logged channels. Computed and applied commands land in the
reserved nav.* group; the dead reckoner logs q^Ÿ (scalar-rst) as its estimate channel. The EKF's richer nav.est.* layout is dened in
Chapter 29.
5. Sensor-validity handling. Components receive each sensor sample
with its validity ag (Chapter 25 semantics) and must skip work keyed to invalid samples; the dead reckoner consumes only the IMU, which is always valid.

 Performance re-gate (exit criterion 10), Pi 5 hardware clause.
The FR-32 ascent target ( 100Ṫ real time, single core) with the full built-in GNC stack in the loop is measured as the ascent_gnc_rt_factor metric of scripts/perf_gate.py, on the committed closed-loop ascent missions/ascent_leo_gnc.toml, and is gated on every nightly
run because it sits in that harness's default metric set. What is deferred
is only the requirement that the measurement be taken on real Pi 5 sili-

nightly ubuntu-24.04-arm leg is the interim aarch64 proxy and is
recorded as a proxy, never as a Pi 5 measurement. The item is registered and fully prepared  mission, metric, and gate all committed and exercised in CI  so qualifying a release against the clause is one scripted command once the hardware exists.
28.6 References
The quaternion-feedback PD law and its stability properties follow Wie [60] and Markley and Crassidis [35], transcribed to the project's D-7 conventions; the strapdown increment composition and the coning-residual bound follow Savage [52] and Titterton and Weston [56]; the ascent geometry is derived in Chapter 23. Full bibliographic details appear in the bibliography.
217

Chapter 29
Reference Error-State EKF and Consistency Gates

29.1 Purpose

This chapter species the built-in reference navigation lter (FR-25): an

error-state (indirect) extended Kalman lter, multiplicative in attitude, that

mechanizes a nominal state from the Chapter 24 IMU increments and cor-

rects it with external-nav-x, star-tracker, and altimeter updates (Chap-

ters 26 and 25). It also denes the estimator acceptance instrumentation

of FR-26: the logged estimate and innovation channels, the NEES and NIS
statistics, and the two-sided 95 % chi-square bounds that star consistency
ev- computes per run and over ensembles  the acceptance instrument for ery estimator this project will ever host, classical or learned. Phase 6 exit

criterion 3 gates the reference lter through ensemble NEES and NIS over

reference a 100-run seeded ensemble. The lter is a

: the simplest standard

formulation, exactly specied, chosen so an independent reimplementation

from this chapter alone reproduces it.

29.2 Assumptions and domain of validity
Assumptions:
1. Fifteen error states. Attitude (3), velocity (3), position (3), gyro
bias (3), accelerometer bias (3), in that order. This is the full observable set for the congured sensor suite: the star tracker observes attitude directly, the nav x observes position and velocity, biases are ob-

218

served through their integrated signatures. Scale-factor and misalignment states are deliberately excluded from the reference lter (they are conguration constants of the truth model, not estimated).
2. Filter dynamics model. The navigator's internal gravity model is the central-body point mass, g^(p) = -ṁ p/ p3. The reference consistency scenario congures the truth environment to the same class
(point-mass gravity, no third bodies, no SRP), so process-model mismatch is zero and the NEES/NIS gates test the estimator implementation, not a model-error budget. Runs against richer truth environments require process-noise ination and are diagnostics, not gates  stated
here so nobody tunes Q to force a gate.
3. Bias model match. The lter models both bias errors as rstorder GaussMarkov with the congured sensor parameters (GM, c)
(equation (24.9))  the reference-implementation stance: the truth model is known. The reference scenario disables the turn-on biases
(g0 = a0 = 0) and the altimeter bias (b = 0), making the lter's
stochastic model exact; enabled turn-on biases add a non-decaying
component the GaussMarkov model absorbs only over t  c, and
such scenarios widen NEES beyond the gate by design.
4. Small-error linearization. Standard EKF validity: attitude errors
 1 rad, position/velocity errors small against the linearization scale of g^. Divergence under gross initialization error is out of scope for the
reference lter.
5. First-order discretization. Transition and process-noise matrices
are the rst-order forms of equation (29.8); adequacy requires t   1, t/c  1, and t small against the orbital dynamics (n t  1, n the mean motion)  all satised by orders of magnitude at the D5 cycle rates (1 Hz to 100 Hz). The Van Loan construction remains
the documented upgrade path if a future regime breaks these conditions [58].
Domain of validity: cycle-synchronous operation on the D-5 schedule with the Chapter 24 increment interface; aiding sensors may drop out arbitrarily (validity ags); the lter never throws inside the loop  a non-nite or non-positive-denite input covariance is a conguration error caught by the FR-15 validator, and the Joseph-form update of equation (29.9) preserves symmetry and positive semi-deniteness against accumulation of rounding.
219

220

Gravity is the one acceleration in (29.3) that no sensor reports: the
accelerometer measures specic force and is identically blind to it. Its con-
tribution is therefore not a measurement the lter transcribes but an inte-
gral the lter must evaluate itself, and the accuracy of that quadrature is the
navigator's own responsibility. Equation (29.3) evaluates it with a predictor-
corrector  an Euler predictor (vŸk, pŸk), then the trapezoidal rule on g^ be-
tween the endpoints  which is Heun's method on the gravitational part of
the dynamics (Hairer, Nørsett, and Wanner [20]), of local order O(t3) and global order O(t2). It costs one additional evaluation of g^ per cycle and
nothing else.

29.3.2 Why the gravity step must be second order

The order of this step is not a free implementation choice, and the reason is

quantitative rather than aesthetic. Replacing the corrector with the explicit

Euler step v^k = v^k-1 + v^kI + g^(p^k-1) t  a rst-order velocity feeding

the second-order position integral, which is also internally inconsistent 

deterministic leaves a truncation error that is

: it is a xed function of the

trajectory, not a random variable, so it accumulates coherently instead of diusing as t, and no term of Q in (29.7) describes it.

Measured noise-free from the true state on the reference consistency sce-
nario of Section 29.3.5 (t = 0.1 s, a 7000 km circular orbit), the rst-order

step diverges from the RK4 solution of the same point-mass dynamics 
the scheme the truth trajectory uses  by 2.63 Ṫ 10-2 m/s in velocity and
0.79 m in position over 60 s. That velocity error is equivalent to a constant unmodelled acceleration of 4.38 Ṫ 10-4 m/s 2, which is 41Ṫ the accelerometer bias GM = 1.08 Ṫ 10-5 m/s 2 the lter carries as a state. The estimator's
own numerical error would then be the largest single term in its error budget,

dominating the instrument errors the lter exists to estimate, and it would do

so while the covariance remained unaware of it  precisely the failure mode

the NEES gate of Section 29.3.5 is built to detect. The predictor-corrector
reduces the same 60 s divergence to 4.7 Ṫ 10-7 m/s and 4.4 Ṫ 10-4 m, an equivalent acceleration of 7.9 Ṫ 10-9 m/s 2  1/1400 of the bias sigma, and

comfortably below every error the lter models.

The requirement scales with scenario duration, which is why it cannot be

discharged by observing that some particular short scenario passes its gate:

the rst-order step's equivalent acceleration is approximately constant, so its
velocity error grows linearly in t while the lter's modelled uncertainty grows as t, and the ratio between them therefore grows without bound. A reim-

plementation that adopts the rst-order step will reproduce this chapter's

221

gates on a short scenario and fail them on a longer one.

29.3.5 Consistency statistics: NEES, NIS, and the chi-square gates
Per FR-26 the lter logs, every cycle, the total-state estimate nav.est.x_hat = [qŸ^ (4, scalar-rst), v^ (3), p^ (3), b^g (3), b^a (3)] (16 values) and the error covariance nav.est.P as the row-major packed upper triangle of the 15 Ṫ 15 matrix (120 values), and, per update, the innovation pair nav.innov.y, nav.innov.S (packed upper triangle) tagged by sensor  all inside the FR-
16 reserved groups, by these names.
The estimation error itself is formed core-side and logged on nav.err:
the lter dierences its nominal state against the truth kinematics and the

224

true in-run bias states of Chapter 24, in its own error conventions  qŸk = q^Ÿk-1  qŸtrue,k per (29.2), canonicalized to the +w hemisphere so the double
cover cannot ip the logged error between neighbouring epochs, and additive
dierences elsewhere.

The n  m reduction. nav.err.e has the state dimension n while P
has the error dimension m, and for this lter those dier (16 against 15).
The evaluator therefore reduces the logged error to the parameterization the covariance describes before forming (29.16). For a quaternion-led error state
 the case m = n - 1, the leading four entries being an error quaternion 
the reduction is the small-angle extraction

(29.15)

with the remaining n - 4 entries passing through unchanged. Any other pairing of n and m is a genuine mismatch and is rejected rather than guessed
at. The statistics (Bar-Shalom, Li, and Kirubarajan [4]) are the normalized estimation error squared and the normalized innovation squared,

k = xTk Pk-1 xk (n = 15),

(29.16)

each distributed n2 at every epoch for a consistent lter. Three aggregations
are computed, of which exactly one gates:

with indicative bounds, because successive er-

rors of one run are serially correlated and the independence assumption

behind chi-square bounds does not hold across time within a run [4].

The eect is large, not marginal, and is measured rather than assumed:

on the exit-criterion-3 ensemble  whose per-epoch statistic lies inside

every the acceptance bounds at

epoch  the per-run interval evalu-

ated at dof = K n admits only 7 of those 100 consistent runs, because

serial correlation inates the spread of Ÿ far beyond the width such an

interval assumes while leaving its expectation at n. The same caveat

applies to any statistic pooled across epochs at dof = N K n. Nei-

ther aggregation is an acceptance gate; equation (29.18) applied across
runs is. A command that gated on either would report FAIL on a lter this chapter certies as consistent, so star consistency prints both

without letting them reach its exit code.

(29.18)

the acceptance form for both NEES (n = 15) and NIS (n = m per sensor). For the exit-criterion-3 ensemble, N = 100: NEES bounds [13.95, 16.09]; NIS bounds [5.34, 6.70] for the nav x (n = 6), [2.54, 3.50] for the star tracker (n = 3), and [0.74, 1.30] for the altimeter (n = 1).

 Epoch coverage against that same interval: the count of epochs
whose ŸN falls inside it. This is the companion criterion to the headline,
sensitive to a defect conned to part of a run that an epoch average
would dilute.

headline The gate is taken in two parts. The

applies equation (29.18) to ŸN

averaged over epochs. Averaging over epochs cannot increase that statistic's

variance above a single epoch's  equality would require perfectly corre-

lated epochs  so judging it against the single-epoch interval is conservative

whatever the across-time correlation is, and it is the criterion that catches a
shifted level: a mis-scaled covariance or a biased estimator displaces ŸN by

a multiple of the interval width.

coverage The

criterion needs a threshold, and the natural-looking choice

is wrong. Under consistency each epoch falls inside a two-sided 95 % interval
with probability q = 0.95, so the count inside is X  Binomial(K, q) with E[X ] = qK: a rule of at least 95 % of epochs inside tests X against its

own mean and a correct lter passes it only about half the time. Measured

on the exit-criterion-3 ensemble, the three NIS statistics landed at 93.3 %,

93.3 % and 95.0 % inside  two of the three would fail a rule they had even

odds of meeting. The threshold is placed in the lower tail of that binomial
instead: at condence c,

t = 1 + max{ j : Pr[X  j]  1 - c }, X  Binomial(K, q), (29.19)

so that Pr[reject | consistent] = Pr[X < t]  1 - c by construction. The default c = 0.999 follows from the instrument's role rather than from convention: star consistency is an automated gate reporting one coverage crite-
rion per statistic  four for the reference lter  so a per-criterion budget of

226

10-3 holds a whole report's spurious-failure rate near 4Ṫ10-3, about one false red in 250 clean runs. At K = 60 this gives t = 51 (Pr[X < t] = 7.4 Ṫ 10-4) and at K = 601, t = 553 (6.7 Ṫ 10-4). The cost in power is small because

genuine inconsistency does not nudge the coverage fraction, it collapses it.

Equation (29.19) gates only where its independence premise holds, and

that is a structural property of the statistic known before any data is seen.

NIS For

it holds exactly: the innovation sequence of a consistent lter is

white [4], so successive epochs are independent. Measured over 20 000 syn-

thetic null trials at K = 60, the spurious-failure rate was 0.0750 % against

NEES the 0.0738 % predicted. For

it fails: the state error is a smooth

trajectory, and averaging across runs does not whiten it, since every run car-

ries the same autocorrelation. Measured on the reference lter, the epoch-

mean NEES series has an integrated autocorrelation time near 30 epochs

 roughly 20 eective samples in a 601-epoch run rather than 601  and

a binomial threshold applied to its inside-count rejected 21 of 40 disjoint

gated consistent 100-run ensembles. The coverage criterion is therefore

for

reported NIS and

for NEES, with the headline gating both.

No eective-sample-size correction is applied to rescue the correlated

case, for two reasons. Such a correction must estimate the autocorrelation

time from the same data it judges, and an error that is stuck or drifting

inates that estimate and so loosens its own threshold; a gate must not

be a function the system under test can move. And measurement shows

no threshold would work regardless: over 40 disjoint consistent 100-run en-

sembles the NEES inside-fraction ranged from 0.100 to 1.000 with a 5th

percentile of 0.363, so any threshold loose enough to admit correct output at
the 10-3 level admits nearly everything. The consequence is stated plainly

rather than hidden: a sustained NEES defect that leaves the epoch average

inside equation (29.18) while pushing many individual epochs out is visible

in the reported coverage number but does not set the exit code. Section 29.5

records a measured instance. Chi-square quantiles are evaluated without

external dependencies (D-12) by the WilsonHilferty transformation [62],

3

p2(k)  k

2 1 - 9k + zp

2 9k

,

z0.975 = -z0.025 = 1.959963984540054,

(29.20)
whose relative error against the exact quantiles is below 5 Ṫ 10-5 for k  300
(veried numerically during drafting)  four orders below the gate widths.
The ensemble driver initializes each run's estimate by perturbing the known
true initial state with a seeded draw from N (0, P0) (attitude via equa-

227

tion (29.2)), so the initial error is distributed exactly as the lter believes  the precondition for NEES consistency from the rst cycle.
29.4 Discretization and implementation
Binding implementation notes for the Phase 6 module:
1. Module and traceability. The lter is a built-in C++ IGncComponent
(navigation role) in the FR-25 registry; star consistency is Pythonside, reading only logs. Source comments echo eq:ekf:qerr, eq:ekf:mech, eq:ekf:errdyn, eq:ekf:F, eq:ekf:disc, eq:ekf:joseph, eq:ekf:stinnov, eq:ekf:altH, eq:ekf:reset, and the consistency evaluator echoes eq:ekf:nees, eq:ekf:nis, eq:ekf:ensemble, eq:ekf:coverage, eq:ekf:wh.
2. Cycle order, normative. (1) mechanize the nominal state, equa-
tion (29.3); (2) propagate the covariance, equation (29.8), with F evaluated at the pre-cycle nominal and the cycle-average ^ , f^; (3) process
valid updates in the xed order nav x, star tracker, altimeter, each as equations (29.9)(29.14) with an immediate reset; (4) log estimate, covariance, and innovations.
3. Linear algebra. Fixed-size Eigen operations only; the S solves use
Eigen::LDLT on the (at most 6 Ṫ 6) innovation covariance  deter-
ministic, no pivoting hazards at these sizes; no heap allocation in the cycle path (D-10). Every Eigen product is bound to a named concrete
type, never auto (the Phase 4 dangling-expression lesson).
4. No truth access. The lter sees only GncInput; the consistency
evaluator, not the lter, consumes truth channels oine. The oracle
ag exists for debugging other components and is never read by the reference lter.
5. Determinism. Same seed, same binary: identical nav.* channels
byte-for-byte; the exit-criterion-3 ensemble rerun is bit-identical because every run's draws come from named streams keyed by the manifest seed schedule.
29.5 Validation evidence
This chapter species two separable pieces, both now implemented. The consistency statistics of Section 29.3.5  equations (29.16), (29.17), (29.18),
228

(29.19), and (29.20)  are implemented in python/star_reacher/consistency.py (with the quantile and binomial evaluators in chi2.py) and are covered by
Table 29.1. The reference error-state lter of Sections 29.129.4 is imple-
mented in cpp/src/gnc/ekf.cpp and is covered by Table 29.2.

Measured sensitivity of the gate. The gate was exercised against delib-

erately broken lters produced by perturbing the reference mission only  no
source change, the same binary  each judged by star consistency over its own 100-run ensemble. An unmodelled gyro turn-on bias (NEES 5.7 Ṫ 103), an unmodelled accelerometer turn-on bias (6.8 Ṫ 103), an unmodelled nav-x
GaussMarkov error (68.0) and a 500 m biased initial estimate (21.0, with
nav-x NIS at 10.97) were all rejected with a nonzero exit code. Against the

same ensembles the covariance-scaling detection oor of the headline crite-

rion at N = 100 is about ḟ7 %, matching the interval half-width: reported

covariance at 0.9Ṫ and 1.1Ṫ truth is caught, 0.95Ṫ and 1.05Ṫ are not.

not Two classes are measured as

caught, and are recorded here rather

than left to be rediscovered. A defect conned to a short transient escapes

both criteria: initializing the lter fourfold over-condent drives ensemble
NEES to 41.7 over the rst ten epochs  far outside the bounds  yet the 601-epoch average is 15.68 and the coverage count 574/601, so both criteria

pass. And a sustained defect that lands just inside the interval escapes the

headline while being plainly visible in the reported coverage number: a 10 m
unmodelled altimeter turn-on bias gives ensemble NEES 15.96 against an upper bound of 16.09 (pass) with coverage 343/601 against an indicative

threshold of 553  the case Section 29.3.5 says the NEES coverage number

reports but does not gate. A campaign that needs either class covered should

gate on a windowed statistic over a segment short enough to resolve the

transient, which is separate work from this chapter's whole-run aggregates.

How the criterion-3 driver reaches its verdict. The driver takes
both halves of the criterion through consistency.ensemble_gate(), the same instrument star consistency uses, rather than reimplementing the
bounds (29.18) beside it. It does so in-process, importing the function directly; it does not shell out to the command line, which is why the CLI rows of Table 29.1 are the sanctioned command-line form of the ensemble gate rather than the path this criterion takes. The two remain tied together because both call one implementation.
The consequence that matters is that the instrument's coverage logic now runs on the criterion-3 path, and it distinguishes the two statistics. NEES

is gated with epochs_independent = False: the epoch coverage fraction is
computed and reported, but excluded from the verdict, which rests on the headline bound alone. That exclusion is structural, made from what the statistic is rather than estimated from the data being judged. The count of
epochs inside is Binomial(n, 0.95) under the null, so a threshold set at 95 %
would test that count against its own mean and a correct lter would meet it about half the time; for NEES it is worse than a coin ip, because the epochmean series has an integrated autocorrelation time of roughly 30 epochs and the count-inside is correspondingly over-dispersed. Such a rule would be green only while the seeds stayed pinned, and any legitimate change perturbing the last bits  a compiler change, a platform with dierent rounding, a model x  would ip it with probability near one half and present as an EKF consistency failure when nothing was wrong.
NIS is gated with epochs_independent = True, where the binomial
premise does hold: a consistent lter's innovations are white, so succes-
sive epochs are independent and consistency.inside_count_threshold
is an exact bound on the spurious-failure probability at the library's de-
fault c = 0.999 rather than a test of the count against its own mean.
Both halves additionally assert that the instrument's interval equals the
one test_ekf_consistency derives independently from this chapter, so a
change to either the chapter or the library is caught here instead of silently shifting the gate.
29.6 References
The error-state (multiplicative) EKF formulation follows Solà [55] and the MEKF heritage in Markley and Crassidis [35], transcribed to the D-7 conventions of Chapter 1; strapdown mechanization terms follow Titterton and Weston [56] and Savage [53], with the predictor-corrector gravity quadrature of Section 29.3.2 following Hairer, Nørsett, and Wanner [20]; GaussMarkov process algebra follows Maybeck [36]; NEES/NIS consistency testing and its chi-square acceptance bounds follow Bar-Shalom, Li, and Kirubarajan [4]; the quantile approximation is Wilson and Hilferty [62]; the rejected higherorder discretization is Van Loan [58]. Full bibliographic details appear in the bibliography.
